We sat down feeling out of place, and after we gave our mumbled introductions, he smiled at us gently.

``You're not that interested in physics, are you? I heard from Watari-kun.''

So he already knew. Mizasaki scratched his head apologetically.

``Yeah\dots\ It's not that we're not interested, honestly---we're just kind of bad at it\dots\ We're more chemistry and biology guys.''

``That's fine. Don't worry about it. Physics and math are the same---if you understand how to handle them as tools, that's more than enough as general education. Not everyone needs to understand the beauty of Euler's identity.''

I'd heard he was the Physics Club President and Student Council President, and that he was second in the grade academically---and on top of that, Mikage Aya's brother---so I'd expected some terrifying prodigy to appear, but he was a very kind person.

``I'm sure you've been told all sorts of things by Watari and the others, but please don't take it seriously. They love talking trash about us.''

As I said that, I glanced toward the entrance. I could see Watari hanging around with his usual two guys, looking our way with grins as they traded jokes.

``Of course. I think I've known your relationship for quite a while.''

``\dots Quite a while?''

Mizasaki echoed. Naturally, Mikage-senpai and we were meeting for the first time today.

``I've been LINE friends with Watari-kun since we met at last year's cultural festival. He's a physics lover---at Tsunanagai First Junior High, he was a standout who fought for the top spot with Delta-kun. There was no way I wasn't going to recruit him to our club. I'd had my eye on him since last year. And since I'd heard various rumors about you guys from him, that's why I called you to the welcome event too.''

To be trying to secure members from that far back---Mikage-senpai really must be serious.

But\dots\ listening to senpai talk, it felt like a bitter taste spread in my mouth.

``It's not like I was competing with Watari. He's just the one who picks fights with me.''

``Come on, don't say that. I know you're actually close.''

As I hesitated, searching for words to object, Mikage-senpai winked and whispered to me.

``By the way, on the entrance exam scores, I believe Delta-kun was top among the local science-track students. You can hold your head high. Watari-kun was close, though.''

So on the last exam, I beat Watari---just as I started to feel relieved, I realized something.

``\dots How do you know that?''

There was no way he should. I hadn't even been told my entrance exam score.

``Well, because I'm Student Council President.''

That wasn't an explanation. Mizasaki's eyes went wide.

``If you're Student Council President, you can view entrance exam results\dots?''

``I'll refrain from saying it explicitly, but---''

With a gentle smile, he raised his index finger and lowered his voice.

``At this school, outstanding students are given that kind of authority and discretion.''

While I stood there stunned, Mikage-senpai spread both hands wide.

``Welcome to the college-prep school where monsters live.''

I had thought there would be nothing to see in the physics lab, but Mikage-senpai guided us to a long table with a glass tank about fifty centimeters wide. The tank was filled about halfway with a white liquid.

``It's water and potato starch mixed at a two-to-three volume ratio. It exhibits an interesting property called dilatancy.''

I'd heard that somewhere before. Thinking back, Iwama had used that word on the back mountain. At this scale, it made sense that they'd used three kilos of potato starch.

Putting on thin vinyl gloves, senpai scooped up the white liquid from the tank.

When he squeezed it tight, the liquid hardened into something like a dumpling. But before long, as if the tension had been released, it slowly returned to a runny liquid.

``You should try it too. Just touching it can kill an hour.''

Mizasaki and I put on vinyl gloves as well and stuck our hands into the tank. It was a strange sensation. If you applied force, it hardened like clay, but if you touched it slowly, it flowed like water.

``Ooh\dots''

``Whoa, this is awesome! What is this!''

A long time ago, I'd played with slime, but this was several times more fun. You could mostly predict how slime would behave, but the movement of this fluid was strikingly counterintuitive. With my hands plunged into the tank absentmindedly, I almost felt like my mental age had dropped by five or six years.

While we were getting excited, senpai brought over a few tools. First was a large brass sphere.

``Take your hands out of the tank for a moment. If I drop this metal ball---almost 500 grams---into the tank, does anyone have a prediction for what will happen?''

Maybe he did similar experiment shows for younger kids, because Mikage-senpai asked in the tone of a kind older brother. I answered with uncomplicated sincerity.

``Won't the bottom of the tank crack?''

``Then let's try it.''

Senpai lifted the brass sphere in front of his chest and dropped it into the tank from higher up than I expected. My breathing stopped. If it fell on your hand, it would have enough force to shatter bones.

The sphere fell with force---and unbelievably, with a small splat against the white surface, it bounced lightly, then stopped in place. After that, it slowly sank into the liquid.

Mizasaki and I clapped in admiration.

``It's a phenomenon you can see in familiar places, like a wet sandy beach. Put simply, as long as you're applying force slowly, it behaves like a liquid, but when force is applied suddenly, the particles' resistance strengthens and it behaves like a solid. If you spread it shallowly across a wide pool, you can even run on the surface.''

Without pause, senpai used a small plastic food container to scoop out just a little of the fluid.

``Now, there are other interesting things you can do with this dilatant fluid. The tool we'll use is this.''

What he pulled from his blazer pocket was a white machine shaped like a kokeshi doll.

``An electric massager.''

Beside me, Mizasaki jolted with a loud clatter.

``A-an electric massager\dots\ in a high school!?''

I didn't know what he was so shocked about. Senpai wore a perfectly matter-of-fact expression, too.

``It's legitimate equipment we bought with club funds. In the first place, what's wrong with this medical device?''

After finishing, Senpai---for some reason---gave a mischievous grin.

``Now then, Mizasaki-kun---what do you think happens if we use this to apply vibrations to a dilatant fluid?''

``Uh, what happens\dots\dots? I feel like anything I say is going to turn into some nasty dirty joke.''

Mizasaki shot a meaningful glance at Mikage. Senpai laughed it off.

``Let's actually try it.''

This Senpai was good at grabbing people's attention. I couldn't help but be curious what would happen next.

Senpai pressed the massager against the bottom of the plastic container and switched it on. A sound like a phone's vibration turned way up echoed, and then a clear change appeared in the fluid.

It was like tentacles crawling up from hell.

Inside the container, the fluid danced wildly. It thinned and stretched upward, raised itself like a cobra, then toppled over and melted away. It didn't just defy intuition---it even looked like some kind of magic.

``It looks alive\dots\dots''

At my words, Senpai nodded with satisfaction and turned the switch off. The fluid immediately calmed down.

``Vibration is, in other words, a continuous series of tiny impacts. By repeatedly firming and loosening locally, you get this kind of strange behavior.''

Senpai pointed the electric massager toward Mizasaki and me.

``Since we've got the chance, would you two help out with a bit of filming?''

``Filming?''

``Yeah. I was going to record a video of these tentacles, but I'm a little short-handed right now.''

``It looks like you've got plenty of club members, though\dots\dots''

``That's the thing---nobody, for some reason, wants to touch this massager.''

And after an exchange like that, we ended up doing the demonstration. Mizasaki held the container firmly with both hands, and I pressed the electric massager to it from underneath. Switch on.

The demonstration was a complete success. Mikage-senpai, who'd been recording on a smartphone, made an OK sign with his fingers, too.

``Alright, last one---smile, and pose!''

Click. In the end, we even got our picture taken.

``It's fine. Don't worry. I won't misuse it.''

I didn't know what you could possibly misuse it for, but that disclaimer was offered anyway.

It was getting close to the time to head home. With the electric massager in one hand, Mikage-senpai briskly explained the clubs to us. But rather than just the Physics Club, he was explaining science-oriented clubs in general.

``At Tsunanagai High School, where math and science education is strong, there used to be five science clubs. The Physics Club, Chemistry Club, Biology Club, Earth Science Club, and Mathematics Club. Collectively, the five were given the name `Faculty of Science.'''

``Faculty of Science? At a high school?''

``That's right, Delta-kun. It means it used to be so big that it could presumptuously call itself a faculty. As wording, it's not `a faculty of science' so much as `science clubs,' but still.''

Mikage-senpai held up five fingers, then folded them down one by one.

``The Mathematics Club merged into the Physics Club due to lack of members. The Earth Science Club turned into the Astronomy Club, then eventually got absorbed into the Physics Club anyway. Now only three remain---physics, chemistry, and biology---but `Faculty of Science' is a convenient label, so it's still used. In June, there's even an event called the Faculty of Science orientation.''

One of the three remaining fingers was bent just slightly.

``Earlier, we took a look at the Biology Club\dots\dots''

When I swallowed the rest of what I was about to say, Senpai nodded sadly.

``Yeah. If they don't get new members this year, the Biology Club will probably be shut down. You experienced it too, didn't you? These days, the fight to recruit members has become brutal. Especially for the Faculty of Science---it's a fight over top students. As a result of my senpai carelessly poaching new students, the Biology Club lost the competition.''

He sighed and continued.

``I'm not saying you have to join the Physics Club. But if you feel like it, at least consider the Biology Club, too.''

Mikage-senpai stifled a yawn and stretched, then pulled his smartphone from his pocket.

``Huh.''

It was Mizasaki who noticed something. He was looking at the strap on Senpai's phone.

Then I noticed as well, a beat later. A handmade cloisonné charm. On a black background, in light blue, it read ``$i$''.

I immediately understood it was paired with the one belonging to Hongo-senpai from the Chemistry Club.

While watching Mikage's reaction, Mizasaki lowered his voice a little and asked Senpai.

``By the way, Senpai---what kind of relationship do you have with Hongo-senpai from the Chemistry Club?''

Mizasaki might have been trying to keep it a secret, but Senpai answered loudly and without hesitation.

``Oh. Nagisa's my girlfriend. You've already met her, right? She's cute, isn't she?''

``Ah, yeah---got it.''

``We're totally in love. People even call us Tsunanagai High School's best couple.''

As he laughed---heh-heh-heh---he showed us his lock screen. In front of a sky framed by cherry blossoms forming a heart shape, the two of them were smiling with their cheeks pressed together.

``Do you know about the Meoto-zakura behind the school? I confessed there last year.''

There, it finally came back to me. The upperclassman couple we'd passed last week while I was climbing the mountain trail with Iwama---those two must have been Mikage-senpai and Hongo-senpai. That was why both of them had looked vaguely familiar.

But more importantly than that, we had something we needed to worry about.

Faced with Senpai's utterly blissful smile, I cautiously glanced over at his younger sister, Mikage.

Her expression was as blank as ever. And yet, I felt as if a terrifying chill were pouring off her entire body. Her expressionlessness had started to look like a Noh mask.

I'd had an idea ever since she'd been calling Hongo-senpai a ``she-fox,'' but it seemed Mizasaki had stepped on that landmine anyway.

Mikage opened her bag with movements like a well-made robot, then, still expressionless, took out a math magazine.

I didn't know if he was oblivious or doing it on purpose, but Senpai walked over to his little sister with a smile.

``Hey, hey, Aya-chan. This isn't the kind of place to be doing drills.''

And then he pressed the electric massager to the back of Mikage's neck and switched it on.

``Hyah\dots!''

Mikage let out an unbelievably cute sound---something you'd never imagine from her usual demeanor---and jerked in reaction. The math magazine slipped from her hands and was tossed out in front of me.

``S-Senpai! How could you do that to your real little sister?!''

Mizasaki's energy was the same as ever. I'd thought it was the kind of heartwarming closeness you only get between siblings, but why was it not okay to use an electric massager on your real little sister?

When I brought my gaze back, the math magazine had landed open on the desk, spread toward me.

A short equation was circled in orange highlighter. Since it was just symbols, I didn't really understand what it meant, but the ``1'' added to the left-hand side was further emphasized with a black ballpoint-pen circle.

Before I could grasp what it meant, Mikage snatched the magazine back up.

The chime rang. It was almost five.

``Oh, it's already this late?''

Mikage-senpai glanced at the clock, then took out his wallet and began rummaging through it. What he pulled out were two coupons.

``Delta-kun, Mizasaki-kun---thanks for coming today. As an apology for holding you up, I'll give you these as a present.''

They were free-coffee coupons for a café in the city.

``The deadline's today. I'll probably be stuck cleaning up and won't be able to go, so if you want, use them together. Of course, if you toss them, I won't hold it against you---do whatever you like.''

I did want to talk with Mizasaki somewhere calmer. We accepted them gratefully.

When I looked out the window, there weren't many clouds in the western sky. The sunset would probably be beautiful today.

When the three of us left the physics room, Mikage suddenly looked at me.

``If you raise the base of the natural logarithm to the power of the product of pi and the imaginary unit, it becomes exactly negative one.''

I thought she'd started chanting a curse. I asked again.

``Huh, sorry\dots\ what was that?''

``The famous Euler's equation. If you raise the base of the natural logarithm to the power of the product of pi and the imaginary unit, it's negative one. The one that's more common is the version where you add one to both sides and make the right-hand side a clean zero.''

As I stood there dumbfounded, Mikage gave a faint smile.

``Delta-kun, you looked like you were curious.''

Only then did it click that she meant the formula from that math magazine.

``Thanks. Yeah, I guess I was a little curious.''

Of course, it wasn't the specific content itself that I was interested in, but\dots

As we walked toward the shoe lockers, Mikage said,

``Thanks for today. For going along with the club recruiting.''

``It's fine, it's fine! It was super fun. Right, Delta?''

``Yeah. I enjoyed it way more than I expected.''

``Exactly. The Physics Club wasn't a club that really fit us, but it was way more interesting than getting dragged to the swim team. And we even learned an unexpected use for elec---potato starch, too.''

Mikage had originally stepped in because her older brother asked her to, and she'd rescued us so he could funnel us into the Physics Club. In other words, we'd been targets. But thanks to that, we avoided getting abducted by the swim team, and we were able to tour three science clubs---the Faculty of Science---without any trouble.

Today had been win-win.

That was what it should have been, but even as I thought that, I realized a vague sense of unease still lingered in my head.

Something about this felt off.

In the first place, why had Mikage-senpai ordered his sister, Mikage, to guide us into the Physics Club?

Senpai had been in contact with Watari Marejou since last year, and he'd known about us through Watari Marejou as well. He'd heard things from that guy, who would spread our bad-mouthing all day long if he could, and Senpai knew full well that both Mizasaki and I were bad at physics---and that there was basically zero chance we'd join the Physics Club.

If that was the case, wasn't it obvious that calling us to the Physics Club's recruitment event would be pointless?

So then, why---

While I was thinking, we reached the shoe lockers. With the time to head home approaching, the upperclassmen didn't come after us even here.

We put our shoes on, but Mikage didn't reach toward the shoe cabinet.

``Huh, Mikage-san, you're not going home?''

``Yeah. Until Oniichan finishes cleaning up, I'm going to the student council room---''

Mikage abruptly cut herself off mid-sentence. Silence. The perceived temperature clearly dropped by at least five degrees.

``\dots Huh, did you hear something?''

At Mikage's feigned-innocent question, Mizasaki and I shook our heads hard in denial.

``Huh? Hear what? I was thinking about nucleophilic substitution reactions, so I didn't notice!''

``\dots Sorry. I was thinking about SN2 reactions too, so I missed it.''

A meaningless excuse that popped out in the moment. Because I blurted out a word I associated with what Mizasaki had said, the two of us ended up communicating without words and, somehow, it became a thing where we just happened to be thinking about the same sort of topic---but even so, Mikage nodded calmly.

``I see. Good. I thought I heard something about an oni, but I guess it was just my imagination.''

Both Mizasaki and I nodded deeply. It must have been our imagination. It had to be.

We left the school as if fleeing.

Sunset was a café we'd often frequented ever since middle school.

Because the name signified `radiance' touching the `grove,' it was called `Sunset.' It stood on a hill overlooking the Pacific, and true to its name, you could watch the sun set in the west beyond the trees, and enjoy an ocean view to the south.

The combination of wide windows that framed the magnificent scenery and a calm interior built around dark-toned wood was impressive enough to be featured in the tourist association's brochures.

A lot of tourists visited, but the prices were reasonable, and slightly pretentious middle and high schoolers like us came here often, too.

When we opened the door, a bell rang, and a female staff member guided us to our seats. It was a familiar face. She probably recognized us, too, at least vaguely, because with a faint smile, she said,

``Welcome,''

and led us to our table. A four-person sofa seat by the window. The sun hung low in the western sky. Soon, we'd be able to see it sink into the seaside forest.

``Huh\dots''

As he wiped his hands with the wet towel, Mizasaki let out a small sound.

``What is it?''

``No, it's just---we always get shown to a two-person table, right? Why a four-person one today?''

Now that he mentioned it, he was right. The only time we got brought to this kind of seat was when we came with family.

The place wasn't full, but there weren't many seats left. And the two-person table right next to us was open, so guiding us there would've been more rational. Normally.

``Maybe it was just the staff member's whim.''

``Well, I guess that happens.''

I pulled out the coupons we'd been given. A one-free-coffee coupon, valid through today. It seemed any type was fine.

Mizasaki spread the menu out on the table.

``It says the Spring Blend is recommended. What about you, Delta?''

``Then I'll go with that.''

``Want to add cake or something? Even if it's free, it feels kind of wrong not paying anything.''

``Yeah. Let's at least order pudding.''

``Got it.''

In the end, we both ordered the Spring Blend and the pudding set. The pudding was the cheapest dessert, and the set was an extra 300 yen on top of the coffee price. According to the rules printed on the free coupon, in this case you could order the set for 300 yen.

The pudding was homemade, though likely prepared in advance. The set arrived without much of a wait.

The Spring Blend was poured into a cherry-blossom-colored cup with a gold rim. When I took a small sip, a light acidity reminiscent of apricots and a luxurious, floral aroma (that was what the menu said) felt pleasant. The firmly baked pudding was richly sweet as always, and it paired well with the coffee.

``You know,''

Mizasaki murmured as he looked down at the sea.

``I can't really put it into words, but\dots\ wasn't today's recruiting kind of weird?''

``Yeah.''

After nodding, I took another sip of the Spring Blend.

``Mikage-senpai should've known we weren't going to join the Physics Club, and yet he used his sister to summon us to the recruiting event. Then he didn't really recruit us at all---he just showed us an experiment and sent us home. I couldn't really understand why he did that.''

``Yeah. And Hongo-senpai was weird, too. It's like she didn't even want to recruit anyone\dots\ Isn't it the era of fighting over members? If she found out we used to be in the Chemistry Club, she should've tried harder to recruit us, but she was kind of halfhearted about it.''

``And she even handed us a crappy report.''

I took it out of my bag and flipped through it again. Unnatural Japanese, and chemical reaction explanations that looked copy-and-pasted. It wasn't just that it wasn't good---if anything, it felt more like a rush job.

``Well, whatever. Maybe Mikage-senpai just wanted to meet us, and maybe Hongo-senpai was tired. Let's take our time and really discuss which club suits us.''

Two guys stopping by a stylish café was, of course, partly because of the free coupons---but more than that, it was because we wanted to have that discussion in a calm place.

``So, Delta---was there any club that met your specs?''

``Don't say it like that. Sure, I wear glasses, but still.''

While drinking coffee, I thought.

``\dots Out of the three we saw today, I think the Biology Club was the best.''

When I said that, Mizasaki nodded as if relieved.

``Same here. Taking care of living things sounds like a lot of work, but if we can research in peace, it's not a bad deal\dots\ and Delta knows a lot about plants. I'd welcome doing something new, too.''

``By the way, what did Mizasaki think of the Chemistry Club? Your hobby is more aligned in chemistry more than biology right?''

``Hmm\dots''

Mizasaki folded his arms and groaned.

``It wasn't bad. The equipment looked solid, and touring factories or limestone caves sounded kinda fun, and Hongo-senpai was super cute.''

``So that's your type.''

``Yeah. I'm basically a gloomy guy, you know. I figured someone bright like that might be nice.''

I didn't think Mizasaki was basically negative at all, but that wasn't the point.

``But still\dots\ how do I put it, it felt like there were way too many people, and the vibe didn't fit.''

``Same.''

He was using the word ``vibe'' to blur it out, but in reality, little things had been pricking at us and making us feel unpleasant.

There was the club captain who showed off a trick turning barley tea transparent, told us to figure out the secret, and yet clearly didn't think we'd get it right. The sloppy booklet that was handed to us with, ``It's good, so read it,'' as if that settled it. The careless way they nearly forgot to explain what they actually did, even though we'd come because we were interested in the Chemistry Club.

For me, who'd been looking forward to it because it was Tsunanagai High School's Chemistry Club, it was honestly disappointing.

I almost wanted them to say they'd been deliberately trying to drive us away.

Yeah, deliberately---

Something about that idea caught on my mind.

Deliberately?

In an instant, a hypothesis took shape. As I thought back, I felt the pieces clicking neatly into place.

I see. If this hypothesis is right, it explains every discomfort I'd felt.

``\dots Mizasaki, can I say something outrageous?''

``Yeah, of course. Delta's outrageous statements are always welcome.''

After reorganizing my thoughts one more time, I said it.

``What if the Physics Club thing and the Chemistry Club thing were all staged?''

Mikage-senpai's invitation to us---who obviously weren't going to join the Physics Club---was deliberate.

The reason Hongo-senpai treated us so crudely even though we were interested in the Chemistry Club was deliberate.

Couldn't it all have been for one hidden purpose?

``Think about it. If it were just you and me, Mizasaki, we wouldn't have gone to tour some Biology Club with nobody there, right? The Physics Club was just an excuse. Mikage-senpai was trying to get us to go check out the Biology Club. And because it'd be a problem if we joined the Chemistry Club, Hongo-senpai acted in a way that would make us have a bad experience.''

Mizasaki froze for a while, looking like he was thinking with pudding still in his mouth. He swallowed and said,

``Yeah, but\dots\ sure, that would explain the weirdness. But why would the Physics Club captain and the Chemistry Club captain go that far for some Biology Club that's about to die out?''

``Because it's about to die out. If nobody joins this year, the Biology Club gets shut down.''

``But that's not the Physics Club's or Chemistry Club's problem\dots\ is it?''

``There's a hint for that. The keychain. You saw it, right? That cloisonné one.''

``Yeah, the matching ones for the best couple. $i$ and $\pi$, right?''

So you thought that too. But what if you're wrong?

``What if it's not a pair, but a set of three?''

``Huh? Why?''

I took a paper napkin and wrote an equation on it with a ballpoint pen.

``This. Euler's equation. Mikage-senpai mentioned it in passing, too.''

\[
e^{i\pi} = -1
\]

It looked simple when written out. Mikage had said it was famous, and Mikage-senpai had called it beautiful. Sure enough, it really was remarkable that an expression made up of just these three symbols would take such a simple value.

``What is that? Makes no sense.''

``I don't know the concrete meaning either. But it was in that math magazine Mikage was reading. Mikage explained it on the way out, remember? Something about raising the base of the natural logarithm to the product of the imaginary unit and pi, and so on and so forth.''

``Yeah, I guess she said something like that.''

``It matches. This equation and those cloisonné straps.''

On the left side of the equals sign on the napkin, there were three symbols. $\pi$ and $i$---and one more.

``When you compare that cloisonné and this equation\dots\ Hongo-senpai's $\pi$ is pi. Mikage-senpai's $i$ is the imaginary unit. So the question becomes: where is the remaining base of the natural logarithm, $e$?''

I was bad at math and didn't like it, but I'd reluctantly learned about natural logarithms because it was a necessary concept for reading ecology papers. I understood that the base $e$---also called Napier's constant---was a special irrational number with convenient properties for handling exponents and logarithms.

``And someone from the Biology Club has that?''

``That's the idea. If the three of them are close enough to make matching straps, then it makes sense they'd talk about helping the Biology Club.''

``Sure, that tracks\dots\ but it's still just a hypothesis, right? We haven't even met the Biology Club person.''

Only then did Mizasaki's eyes snap wide open.

``Wait, Delta---I've seen an $e$ strap.''

Mizasaki has a good memory for things he's seen once. Looking excited, he worked his smartphone, then---

``Found it!''

He raised his voice, then lowered it when he noticed the people around us.

``Look at this! This photo!''

On Mizasaki's phone was a group photo of the club members we'd seen in the biology room. It was the one displayed at the very top of a simple club-introduction page. Now that I thought about it, Tokumura-sensei had said the album photos were also posted on the website.

``This person---she was the current captain, that Karato girl, right?''

Mizasaki zoomed in on a female student with glasses and messy hair. From her pocket---

``$e$.''

I almost let my own voice get too loud.

Dangling from her pocket was a cloisonné charm---black with a pale green ``$e$'' on it.

``Ha-ha, nice work. So they really were a close trio.''

Mizasaki sat back with a satisfied look.

The three symbols that appear in Euler's equation. They'd used them as the motif for handmade straps, and wore them like this, cherished. Mikage-senpai, the Physics Club President. Hongo-senpai, the Chemistry Club President. And Karato-senpai, the Biology Club President---if those three were close enough to be doing this, it was easy to imagine they weren't connected in any ordinary way.

And I'd heard another line that backed it up.

``There was something else, too---something that showed our recruitment was premised on the relationship between those three. Mizasaki, do you remember what Mikage-senpai said?''

I repeated it aloud.

---Aya-chan, thanks for your plus-one work today

``What do you think it meant?''

``Hm\dots\ I dunno. Like, thanks for doing extra work, I guess?''

``Normally, if someone says `plus one,' that's what you'd think. But apparently Euler's equation also has another way of being written, with a small transformation.''

Beneath the formula on the paper napkin, I added the transformed version.

\[
e^{i\pi} + 1 = 0
\]

``In Mikage's magazine, this version was emphasized, and the `plus one' part was circled. Maybe they were having some strategy meeting---like, `Okay, Aya-chan is this 1.' When Mikage-senpai made that plus-one remark, you could take it to mean Mikage was in the position of cooperating with the three third-years.''

``Ah\dots\ yeah, I see.''

Mizasaki took a sip of coffee with a grave look, then continued.

``So we got invited by Mikage-senpai using the Physics Club as an excuse, and we went to the new-member fair. And then, naturally, we ended up stopping by the Biology Club---somewhere we were supposed to pass by without visiting. We politely turned down the Chemistry Club, which had been a candidate. In other words, we were being carefully guided into thinking it'd be best to join the Biology Club.''

``Yeah, there's a lot of inference in it. And it still leaves questions---like why Karato-senpai herself wasn't there if they wanted to bring in members. And unless we hear it from Mikage herself, we can't know what they intended when they called us over---''

I cut myself off as I noticed yet another oddness.

Would something like this really happen by coincidence today? No---

Just then, I caught sight of the name tag of a female staff member passing near our table. I still didn't have my thoughts fully organized, but I decided to act anyway.

``Mizasaki---can I move over to that seat for a second?''

I pointed to the spot beside Mizasaki on the sofa.

``Huh? Uh, sure.''

``I'm moving the bags over here.''

``Be my guest.''

I moved Mizasaki's bag to my side and set it next to mine. Then I sat in the newly opened spot beside Mizasaki.

``Heh\dots\ this is kinda embarrassing. Feels like we're a couple.''

``\dots The sunset's really beautiful.''

``Your heart's even more beautiful, Delta.''

After our ritual-like joking around, I returned to my side as if nothing had happened. Mizasaki's bag stayed on this sofa.

``So what was that just now?''

Mizasaki asked, and I answered with a silent smile. If my prediction was wrong, it'd be embarrassing, so I decided not to say it yet.

Besides, I still didn't know why this was being done.

Watching the sun sink, I started on the rest of my pudding.

The door chime rang, and Mikage Aya entered the café right around when I finished the last bite.

``What a funny coincidence. Mind if I sit here?''

Saying something so blatantly insincere, Mikage sat down next to Mizasaki. She didn't sit next to me because two people's bags were piled there. Meanwhile, on Mizasaki's side, there was an empty space---the one I'd made earlier for myself.

With a female classmate sitting beside him, Mizasaki hunched his shoulders shyly.

I couldn't help smiling. I was sure it was a bad smile.

``Hey, Delta---why---don't tell me\dots\ you came over to sit next to me earlier for this?''

I chose not to answer that. If I had to put it into words, it was a small bit of payback for the cherry blossoms.

Once Mikage's café latte arrived, I finally got to the main point.

``\dots There's something we have to ask you, Mikage-san.''

``I had a feeling I was going to get asked something.''

So we told Mikage what we'd pieced together from our conversation.

The discomfort we'd felt at the Physics Club and the Chemistry Club.

The cloisonné straps and Euler's equation.

The hypothesis that Mikage's actions were meant to steer us toward the Biology Club.

When we finished, Mikage slowly---deeply---bowed her head.

``I'm sorry.''

Mizasaki panicked.

``H-hey, Mikage-san, you don't have to---don't bow your head like that.''

``No. This is something I should apologize for properly. Your hypothesis is correct.''

When she raised her head, she pulled the math magazine---the one in question---out of her bag.

``You realized it after seeing this.''

``\dots Yeah.''

``As expected of you, Delta-kun. This magazine was a present from senpai. I received it when I heard about the plan.''

She'd kept it vague with ``senpai,'' but it was almost certainly Mikage-senpai---her older brother---who'd bought onigiri for Mikage Aya. Maybe this was her tactic to avoid accidentally calling him Oniichan at school by using a more formal label.

With long, slender fingers, she opened it to the page where Euler's equation was emphasized.

``I was told that there were marks on this equation. If I joined---like the 1 added to the left side---the plan would be complete. That's what my brother told me, and I decided, reluctantly, to become part of the plan.''

Because it was a request from the brother she loved, she probably couldn't refuse. I felt a little sorry for her.

``For Karato-senpai, who had completely lost motivation, we tried to guide you two toward the Biology Club. We wanted you to see the Biology Club. I'm truly sorry for doing something that amounted to lying.''

The last light of the sunset lit Mikage's profile.

With her bowing her head to me, I searched for how to put this feeling into words.

``It's not like it was a lie, exactly. But\dots\ if you wanted us to join the Biology Club, wouldn't it have been better to just tell us honestly from the start?''

At my words, Mikage lifted her face and looked straight at me.

``Because the Biology Club is unpopular and on the verge of collapsing, we want you to consider joining---like that?''

When she put it that way, I had to admit she was right. If she said something that felt like making us draw the short straw, it could push us away instead. Or rather---it probably would have pushed us away. Trying to shove a club on the brink of collapse onto us would come off as insulting. No thanks to the Biology Club---we'd find a club that suited us ourselves. That was the kind of people Mizasaki and I were.

So I could understand the idea of pretending to recruit us for the Physics Club and casually getting us to look at the Biology Club, too. Even so, it was a very roundabout love letter.

``Still\dots\ it actually made me kinda happy.''

Mizasaki said it gently.

``Like, I could feel how serious you were. If you went that far because you really wanted us to join the Biology Club, it kinda makes me feel like\dots\ maybe I wouldn't mind joining.''

Mikage slowly shook her head.

``You don't need to consider me. I deeply regret pulling a scheme like this. I want you to join the club you truly want to join.''

There was a brief silence. I took the last sip of my coffee.

After setting my cup down, I met Mizasaki's eyes. We were thinking the same thing.

``We're joining. The Biology Club.''

``Yeah. It's decided.''

I turned to Mikage, who had pressed her lips together tightly.

``This isn't like we're doing it out of mercy for you, Mikage-san. We're making this decision because we want to---on our own.''

``\dots Thank goodness.''

Smiling as if the tension had drained out of her, Mikage boldly downed her café latte, which still looked hot.

We parted ways with Mikage, who said she was headed in the opposite direction, and started home. It was already spring, but the night wind blowing up from the sea was still a little cold. The dark trees rustled as they swayed.

I was still silently thinking about what that waitress's behavior had meant.

Apparently, that incident had lingered as a sense of unease for Mizasaki, too.

``Hey, Delta---how did you predict that seat thing, anyway?''

That ``seat thing'' was the part where Mikage ended up sitting next to Mizasaki. It had been just in case, but I'd moved Mizasaki's bag to my side with the possibility in mind that Mikage might show up. To carry out a small revenge---having Mizasaki sit next to a girl, as payback for the cherry blossom incident.

The one who noticed was you, Mizasaki. We always got shown to a table for two, but today, for some reason, it was a table for four. While I was thinking about why, it occurred to me---maybe.

``Maybe what?''

``If there was a reason the waitress who normally seats us at a two-person table guided us to a four-person table, then one possibility is that she was anticipating the presence of one more person.''

``One more---wait, are you saying that waitress could see a third person!?''

``That's not what I mean. I mean she was taking into account the possibility that someone else would join later.''

There was a pause long enough for him to think.

``Yeah, but that doesn't make sense. We didn't say a single word about Mikage-san coming later, and honestly, I wasn't even expecting it.''

``That waitress's name tag said `MIKAGE.'''

``Huh\dots?''

``She's probably a relative of Mikage or Mikage-senpai. She must've gotten word from one of the siblings that one more person would come after us.''

``Hold on---no way. I mean, Mikage-san couldn't have known we were going to Sunset---''

Mizasaki cut himself off.

``Right. We came to Sunset because Mikage-senpai gave us free-coffee coupons that were valid through today. If that's the case, it's not hard to predict we'd show up at Sunset at some point today.''

``But how did that waitress even identify us? We didn't exactly announce our names when we walked in.''

``We got photographed. During the dilatancy experiment.''

``Ah\dots''

Mikage-senpai had taken photos of the two of us today. He could've sent them to the staff member and asked, ``If these two come in, Aya-chan will join them later, so please seat them at a table for four.''

The sky was completely dark now. The road home was dotted with pools of light from white streetlamps.

``I get that it's possible in theory, but\dots\ why would they go that far?''

``Yeah. That's the real issue---why they did it.''

I'd been thinking about it the whole time. It was easy to infer the facts: the staff member named Mikage seated us at a four-person table as groundwork for Mikage Aya arriving later. But the motive---why they did it---was still in the dark.

What did Mikage accomplish by having coffee with us?

It felt like pushing through a dark thicket.

Depending on the answer, today's events might be fundamentally overturned.

After walking for a while and organizing my thoughts, I voiced one theory.

``Today's mystery-solving was just\dots\ too well-constructed, wasn't it?''

``\dots What do you mean?''

I raised my index finger.

``Don't you think the clues were a little too complete---necessary and sufficient? Senpai's straps. Was saying what was staged wasn't just up to the point we left it really a coincidence that everything was presented in a way that made sure we'd notice?''

I counted a second point with my finger.

``And then there was the math magazine---the one with an equation that hinted at `one more' beyond that. Mikage-senpai used the electric massager on Mikage, and the magazine got tossed right in front of me. And right there was the equation we needed as a clue, with the relevant part emphasized so it stood out. Does that really just happen by chance?''

The clues had been laid out for us---like mouthwash and vitamin C placed casually on a table.

``Whoa, are you saying even that whole skit was staged?''

``And third---most importantly---there was the existence of someone who guaranteed our mystery-solving. Without someone to corroborate it, the club-recruitment maneuver would've been nothing but our guesswork and delusions. But Mikage coming to Sunset and admitting everything let us be sure it was real.''

And then---

``That's exactly why we accepted senpai's feelings and decided to join the Biology Club, isn't it?''

Staring at the three fingers I had raised, Mizasaki went speechless.

``Even the opportunity for Mikage to confess her scheme might have been carefully prepared---through the free coupons, the staff member, and the four-person table. That means we were provided with all the information we needed to be confident the recruitment maneuver existed. This mystery is\dots\ too beautiful.''

``So you're saying what was staged wasn't just up to the point we left school\dots\ but all the way until we solved the mystery at Sunset and did the answer check with Mikage-san?''

``You could think of it that way. This is nothing more than speculation, but it's possible that the whole arc was calculated: we deduce it, we see through the truth, Mikage-san gets her confession in---and then we feel like, `If you went that far, we'll join the Biology Club,' all as the intended endpoint.''

``No way\dots\ that's gross. You're overthinking it, Delta.''

``\dots Maybe.''

I wanted to believe that.

Because if someone could calculate even what was inside our hearts, they'd have to be a monster.

% ==============================
%        Fragment
% ==============================
\clearpage
\thispagestyle{plain}
\phantomsection
\begin{center}
    \large\bfseries
    Fragment\\
    \textit{Cerasus × yedoensis} ``Somei-yoshino''
\end{center}
\label{sec:fragment1}
\addcontentsline{toc}{chapter}{Fragment}
\vspace{1cm}

I thought cherry blossoms ought to bloom with their chests held high.

Because they carried that much expectation.

The town was as crowded as it got all year. Not even Golden Week or summer vacation drew this many people. I was surprised to hear that, at peak bloom like this, people even came all the way from out of the prefecture.

It was spring break. I lived here locally. I should have been able to aim for a quiet weekday. And yet the reason I ended up going out on a Sunday afternoon---guaranteed to be packed---was simply because of my younger sister's selfishness.

``It's more fun when there are lots of people. It feels more like a festival.''

Whether it was fun or not was a difference in values. So I couldn't argue her into submission.

My father had said, ``You and Asahi, go on,'' and shoved three thousand-yen bills into my hands. My parents went off to work just like that, and I came to view the cherry blossoms with my younger sister.

We had come to see the cherry blossoms in full bloom---so full it felt like they were covering spring itself.

I wasn't good with crowds. I hadn't been looking forward to it, but once I was actually out in town, it really was beautiful.

The rows of cherry trees lined up along the embankment of the Tsuna River, which flowed into the Pacific, were dyed a pale pink as if someone had scattered watercolor paint across the sky. Even a light breeze sent petals---too many to count in tens of thousands---swirling through the air. If the wind were strong, it would probably reach into the hundreds of millions.

The road that ran from Hachiman Bridge over the Tsuna River toward the center of town was called Sakura Street. Cherry trees had been planted on both sides in overwhelming numbers, and when they bloomed, it became a tunnel so thick with flowers you couldn't even see the sky. That tunnel guided the feet of the people walking along the river toward Tsunanagai Hachiman Shrine.

Apparently, wealthy people back in the Taisho era had planted them competitively. Within the shrine's spacious grounds, countless impressive Somei-yoshino trees spread their branches wide. It had been worth pushing through the crowd to get here. The cherry blossoms made me feel that way.

Since we were at a shrine, we couldn't exactly just look at the blossoms and leave. My younger sister and I got in the long line that led to the worship hall. As if she'd been waiting for this, my younger sister started stuffing her cheeks full of the sakura domyoji I'd bought in anticipation of the wait. Dumplings over flowers. The younger sister who had chosen the crowd herself but hated standing in line had gone completely quiet, thanks to the sakura mochi. Just as I'd planned.

And then, a man's voice from up ahead caught my interest.

``We should properly give thanks for getting into Tsunanagai High School, too.''

It seemed there was someone a little ahead in line who would be my classmate in the future.

``Of course!''

The reply was a crisp, clear girl's voice. It had to be the man's daughter. From over the shoulders of the people in front of me, I guessed the ponytail I could see belonged to the owner of that voice. On either side were people who looked like her parents.

In the crowd, I couldn't really make out what was going on. But on the hair tie that held her hair up high at the back of her head, there was a distinctive ornament shaped like a cherry blossom. The material was fabric. It was finished three-dimensionally with tsumami zaiku. ``Cherry blossom pink'' often turned into a cheap-looking pink once it became a product, but her cherry blossom wasn't like that. It was a soft, elegant shade that made you feel a kind of respect for nature.

The cherry blossom girl was swallowed up by the crowd again almost immediately.

I accepted the last sakura domyoji from my younger sister, voiced my displeasure that it was half-eaten, savored spring through the refreshing fragrance of the salted cherry leaf, and then finished my visit.

While we were heading back along the approach, I spotted that tsumami zaiku cherry blossom again.

Once again, all I could see was the back of her head. She was facing a long table set up for writing ema, sitting there with a deep, unwavering focus. I couldn't even see her face, but her seriousness came through.

``Hey, want to try writing an ema or something?''

While I used that as an excuse to my younger sister, I pushed through the crowd toward the long table. Just a small spark of curiosity. What would a girl who'd soon be my classmate wish for, in cherry blossom season?

``Huh? Nah. I'm good. It costs money, and it's a hassle.''

Fixating on ema here wasn't really in character for me. ``Yeah, fair,'' I said, changing course.

The cherry blossom girl seemed to have finished writing her wish, and started moving from the long table over to the ema rack. I flicked my eyes toward her, and instantly felt embarrassed. Even if it was meant to be seen, trying to peek at someone else's wish was the height of bad taste. And besides, it was a girl's wish.

I looked away immediately---looked away, I did, but even so, I accidentally caught sight of what she had written, and it burned into my retina like a harsh flash. It was just a single sentence, but it was a wish completely unlike anything I had expected.

Beautiful handwriting that made you feel her education. And precisely because of that, the strangeness of the content stood out even more.

\textbf{In high school, I hope I can do well.}

% ==============================
%        Chapter 3
% ==============================
\clearpage
\thispagestyle{plain}
\phantomsection
\begin{center}
    \large\bfseries
    Chapter 3\\
    Sho Does Not Speak
\end{center}
\label{sec:ch3}
\addcontentsline{toc}{chapter}{Chapter 3}
\vspace{1cm}

Iwama became a class favorite in the blink of an eye.

You could tell how smart and efficient she was just by watching her run homeroom. That monstrous stamina---taking on every job while using her ``class rep'' title as a shield, yet never showing the slightest fatigue. And above all, that cherry-blossom-like charm that drew people in regardless of gender.

If you told everyone to point at the class representative on the count of ``one, two,'' thirty-nine out of forty students in Class 1-C would point at Iwama without a doubt. The remaining one---Iwama herself---would think for only a few milliseconds before probably pointing at the other class rep. He was a pretty good guy too, but unfortunately, he was no match for Iwama.

From the corner of the back row on the hallway side to the center of the classroom. That was a metaphorical expression---there hadn't been any seat changes---but in practice, Iwama stopped taking it easy at her own desk altogether.

Naturally, I had fewer chances to trade words with Iwama. Even so, every morning she still called out brightly, ``Morning!'' and when I passed the handouts around, she still whispered, ``Thanks.'' Somehow, anything more than that started to feel hard for me, and in a reversal of how it used to be, I found myself making more trips over to Mizasaki's seat instead.

In the end, I still didn't really know what Iwama planned to do about clubs. After that conversation we'd had right before club recruitment officially opened up, I never talked with Iwama about choosing a club again.

Since then, I'd seen a girl who looked like a middle-school friend of hers come into the classroom to pass along some message to Iwama. They'd waved at each other with a ``See you after school'' kind of vibe, so her feelings were probably settling toward the basketball club.

That time we climbed the back hill together to see the cherry blossoms had to have been something like an illusion.

Or else a rare collision accident---like two butterflies knocking their foreheads together.

Iwama often stood up front to speak, but unless it was math class, she never carelessly used words like ``uniqueness,'' and she never called out things like, ``Split up by group and discuss it\dots\ scientifically!''

I wondered if she'd thrown away the katakuri, caked in dirt and stuffed into a filthy plastic shopping bag. If she'd kept it somewhere out of misplaced consideration, I felt bad---but there was no way to check.

The last message history on my LINE with Iwama was still that exchange about the photo.

``Come to think of it, I haven't talked to Iwama-san lately.''

In the middle of lunch, Mizasaki suddenly started saying that. In his line of sight, on nearly the opposite side of the classroom, was Iwama chatting and laughing. Mizasaki's seat was in the back by the windows.

``If it bothers you, why don't you go talk to her?''

``Nah, it's rough if Delta won't stay with Iwama-san, you know? Like, I'm basically socially awkward, right? Without a reason, it's hard to start talking to her.''

He was trying to say, indirectly, ``Lately Delta hasn't been with Iwama-san, has he?'' What needless meddling.

``Don't expect that from me. If there's a seat change, I won't even have any point of contact with her anymore.''

``But, Delta-kun.''

The one who reacted wasn't Mizasaki, but Mikage Aya in the seat in front of me. She turned around toward us with hand-rolled sushi in hand.

``I heard from a certain source that the other day, Delta-kun was seen climbing the back hill with Iwama-san, the two of you getting along.''

``Huh, seriously?! That huge of an incident?!''

They were both being obvious. Mizasaki had to know perfectly well it was the result of his own scheme, and Mikage's ``certain source'' was almost certainly her older brother---Mikage-senpai.

When I glared at him, Mizasaki blatantly changed the subject.

``Oh yeah, and I heard someone saw a person who looked like Iwama-san at the new bookstore that opened in the central shopping district.''

``Iwama-san would stop by a bookstore, sure.''

``I heard it while I was gathering intel on cute girls in other classes---someone said they saw this super cute girl in our uniform at the bookstore. It's only a matter of time before the world finds out about Iwama Rio, huh.''

How could he talk about ``cute girls'' like that right in front of a girl?

``So that person didn't know who Iwama-san was?''

Mikage, too, looked interested as she asked Mizasaki. True enough---if you already knew what Iwama looked like, you probably wouldn't describe her as ``a girl wearing our uniform.''

``Yeah, yeah. When I asked about the features, it sounded a lot like Iwama-san. The class badge said 1-C. And her skirt was knee-length, and she had a ponytail.''

Still facing Mizasaki, I shifted only my eyes to indicate Mikage. Mikage's skirt was a little longer than knee-length, and though it was a different style, she had a ponytail too. It was a warning: if he kept going, he'd be implying, without saying it outright, that Mikage wasn't ``super cute.''

``Oh, and what was it again\dots\ she said she had this smile like a flower blooming\dots''

Hearing that, Mikage put on a bright, cheerful smile that didn't suit her.

``Then it might be Iwama-san.''

If she was doing it on purpose to mess with Mizasaki, I fully supported it.

Mizasaki panicked at Mikage's smile.

``A-and, um, what else was it\dots\ oh, yeah---she was chatting happily with a short girl, apparently. With a girl who had headphones hanging around her neck.''

I see. In that case---

``If that's it, then it feels like it should be uniquely determined as Iwama-san.''

Mikage's comment had been made with her in mind---someone who spoke to almost no one but Iwama.

Kannabi Rei was a girl who gave off a black aura.

Words like ``plain'' or ``unremarkable'' didn't really fit. It wasn't that kind of faint impression---rather, it was as if she wore a pitch-black curtain that kept people away.

She was small and slender. Her black hair was cut straight around her neck, and her bangs were long enough to hang over her eyes. On top of that, she always kept her head slightly lowered, so you could hardly see her face.

In the morning short homeroom, until our homeroom teacher arrived, and in the afternoon short homeroom, after our homeroom teacher left, Kannabi wore headphones. Of course, inside the school she only kept them hanging around her neck, but on the way to and from school, she seemed to have them on her ears. They worked like a ward, and no one went out of their way to talk to her.

Except for one person: Iwama Rio.

Since Kannabi's attendance number came right after Iwama's, her seat was in the very front of the second row from the hallway. You couldn't say that was close to Iwama, who sat in the back. Even so, the reason Iwama often went over to talk to Kannabi was probably because there was no one around Kannabi. The kind of consideration you'd expect from a class rep. Probably.

Even I---whose attendance number was close---and Mizasaki, who was relatively good socially, had never had a conversation with Kannabi.

There was no reason to talk to her in the first place. And it was supposed to stay that way from here on out, too, but---

Friday after school, as the week when club recruitment had opened was coming to an end.

Kannabi suddenly showed up in the Biology Room, for some reason.

Mizasaki and I had experienced that bizarre ``recruitment'' on Monday, and the next day, Tuesday, we submitted our club-joining forms for the Biology Club. The poster in front of the Biology Room said the club's regular activity days were Monday, Wednesday, and Friday. So we tried to stop by on Wednesday, but the Biology Room wasn't even unlocked, and Tokumura-sensei was away at a staff meeting. Then, when we came back to the Biology Room again on Friday, we found Kannabi sitting there all alone.

``H-huh? Kannabi-san?''

Mizasaki reacted first after opening the door. Kannabi looked our way and seemed like she was about to say something, but---

``\dots Ah, uh\dots\ um, well\dots''

After her mouth moved like that, she ultimately said nothing, and lowered her gaze again.

If she was in the Biology Room at this hour, she probably had some interest in the Biology Club, but with her just sitting there, it was hard to tell.

The ear that peeked out slightly from between her black hair was bright red. If you wanted to be kind, you'd call her shy; if you wanted to be unkind, she seemed socially awkward. As for me, sure---but Mizasaki was the type who could talk relatively well, and even he seemed unable to find the right words for this kind of situation, with this kind of person, so he ended up offering only a strangely formal greeting.

``Excuse us.''

Tokumura-sensei was apparently away from school for work again today. As a result, a painfully awkward situation occurred: just the three of us in the Biology Room---me, Mizasaki, and Kannabi.

For the record, Karato, the only upperclassman, never showed her face during activities at all. We hadn't even seen her around. According to Tokumura-sensei, she took care of the animals in the morning or during lunch break, then promptly went home after school.

Kannabi, at least, didn't have her headphones on her ears, but she stayed seated in silence, continuing to write something in her notebook. I couldn't tell whether it was okay to talk to her. Meanwhile, to avoid the room turning into the atmosphere of a wake, Mizasaki and I resumed our discussion about optical isomers.

But of course, neither Mizasaki nor I thought it was fine to leave things like that.

``Right---let's do introductions or something.''

After that budgerigar let out a ``Samishii ne\dots'' and the air loosened for an instant, Mizasaki forced the declaration into the opening and stood up. The timing was good. I nodded along.

``My name is Izuta Sho. My strong subject is biology, and my weak subject is math. My last name is written with the kanji for `to come out' and `rice paddy,' so my close friends call me Delta. I'd be happy if you'd call me Delta too!''

Kannabi turned toward us and froze. Sure, he'd succeeded in getting her attention, but that attention was more like, ``What is this guy even saying?''

The room went dead silent. Only the budgerigar reacted, letting out a chirp that sounded like it was snickering through its nose.

``Why did Mizasaki do my self-introduction?''

At my protest, Mizasaki replied breezily.

``Huh? Because it's funnier that way.''

Unfortunately, Kannabi wasn't laughing at all.

``---Anyway, putting that little skit aside, I'm Mizasaki Ryuichi. I'm hoping to become the one who leads this club as a pilot with exceptional comedic sense. Nice to meet you!''

Kannabi didn't move.

``Also, `Mizasaki' is kind of a mouthful, so you can call me Ryuichi if you want.''

No one reacted anymore. After a brief pause---

``Wait, why is Mizasaki doing the self-introduction?''

Mizasaki lightly tapped my head.

``I didn't.''

``Didn't you?''

I didn't have the sense to imitate Mizasaki and do introductions like him, and I especially didn't have the sense to make surname puns or try to get a girl I'd barely met to call me by a nickname.

It felt like the Biology Room's atmosphere had been completely killed off by that ``exceptional comedic sense.''

Seriously---what was I supposed to do with this.

``Uu\dots\dots\dots\dots snrk.''

I heard a voice and looked over at Kannabi.

Maybe Mizasaki's joke finally landed, or maybe the pointless back-and-forth loosened her up---Kannabi twisted her lips without losing her blank expression, her shoulders trembling slightly. The girl who'd been wrapped in that black veil was laughing.

As if she'd resigned herself to it, Kannabi finally lifted her face properly. From behind her bangs, upturned eyes peeked out---sharper-looking than I'd expected.

``I'm Kannabi Rei\dots\ I joined the Biology Club. I, um\dots\ it's nice to meet you.''

This might have been the first time I'd heard her voice clearly. During self-introductions in the classroom, she'd spoken so softly I couldn't really make it out. It was slightly husky---oddly pleasant to the ear.

In the end, our first day of club activities wrapped up with the small results of self-introductions and exchanging contact info.

The problem was that night.

---Sorry to ask so soon. If you don't have plans, could you show me around Tsunanagai tomorrow?

I'd gotten a message like that from Kannabi, addressed to me personally.

Thrown off by how sudden it was, I still agreed, since I didn't have anything scheduled. As classmates in the Biology Club---only three of us total---it was probably important to deepen our relationship.

---Should I ask about Mizasaki's schedule too?

When I sent that as a follow-up, a reply came almost immediately.

\fullpageimage{4.jpg}


\thispagestyle{plain}

\vspace{1cm}

---No. That's fine.

That probably meant Kannabi had adjusted things on her end. Since she'd said it was fine, I figured there was no need to go out of my way to double-check, so I entered the schedule she'd given me into my calendar.

Meet at 12:00 p.m., Tsunanagai Station North Exit ticket gates.

And the next day, I ended up bitterly regretting not checking.

The air was crisp and clear, as if it stretched all the way up into the sky, and it was so sunny the sun itself felt dazzling.

Tsunanagai Station's North Exit had a small bus rotary, and banks and restaurants lined the area around it. A lot of middle- and high-schoolers who commuted by train tended to hang out at the family restaurants around here. Which was exactly why locals like me and Mizasaki didn't really use them.

From there, the street running north was a station-front shopping district, with specialty stores lining both sides. The customers skewed older, and maybe because of that, the shopping street had bus stops set up at absurdly short intervals. Elderly people got on and off all the time, so it was basically a local bus that made every stop. That was why we didn't use buses much either. Bikes were overwhelmingly faster.

For the record, on the south side of the station, once you crossed the bypass, it was immediately the ocean.

Since it was a day off, the area in front of the station was lively. For a station with only a single line running through it, it was pretty crowded. Not as packed as cherry blossom season, but I could still spot people who looked like tourists. There were plenty of places to enjoy---shrines and temples, seaside parks, and the like.

I stood by the wall so I wouldn't be in anyone's way, waiting for Kannabi and Mizasaki.

A train arrived, and people flooded out from the ticket gates all at once. In that stream, I spotted someone I hadn't expected to see.

``Ah, Del-chan!''

The one waving at me with a way of addressing me I'd never heard before was---Iwama Rio.

She was in casual clothes. A white shirt with a light beige knit layered over it, and a violet-colored culotte skirt on the bottom. On her feet were sporty black sneakers. Compared to her uniform, it gave her a more casual impression, but her overwhelmingly model-student aura was perfectly intact.

Normally I would've greeted her with ``Morning,'' but it was almost noon, so I couldn't use that one. For now, I gave a small nod and let out an ``ss''---the kind of sound you make when you mean ``hey.''

I'd thought it was just a chance encounter, but Iwama came up to stand next to me.

``It's such nice weather. Thank goodness!''

``Ah, yeah\dots''

The uncertainty plainly seeped into my face.

From Iwama's tone, it seemed she recognized me as her companion for today's outing. But I had absolutely no idea what she meant.

Which led to a simple conclusion. Kannabi had invited Iwama. Her message to me hadn't mentioned Iwama at all, but\dots\ could something like that really happen if you thought about it normally?

A communication mistake? When you called someone out on a day off, could you really forget to mention the other members?

Not a mistake, but intentional? If so, was Kannabi the kind of girl who pulled the same sort of thing as Mizasaki?

\dots Putting that aside, there was something I wanted to confirm.

``By the way, that way of calling me---''

``Huh? Calling you?''

Why was she so surprised? We weren't in the kind of relationship where she'd call me that.

``That `Del-chan' thing from earlier.''

``Oh, Rei told me\dots\ sorry, did you not like it?''

Iwama's eyebrows drew a neat inverted V. That straightforward expression caught me off guard.

``It's not like I dislike it\dots''

``Then Del-chan it is! And you don't have to add -san for me either.''

Before I even understood what was happening, the mysterious way of addressing me had been decided. Was this also Kannabi's doing? I'd pictured her as a quiet girl who didn't talk much, but if she was doing all of this on purpose, I needed to rethink that. If she was someone who hid the outing's members, then making up someone else's nickname without permission wasn't exactly impossible. Still, ``Del-chan,'' huh\dots

``\dots So where are we going today, again?''

To get a grasp on the situation, I tossed out a deliberately vague question. It worked whether Iwama was supposed to be acting together with us, or whether she was supposed to be doing her own thing.

``You're showing me around, right, Del-chan?''

``Ah, yeah, right.''

It was true---I'd been asked, ``Could you show me around?'' and I'd answered YES. I had, but I never imagined it was being entrusted to me to this extent.

More importantly, why was I going out with Iwama on a day off in the first place? We were supposed to be nothing more than classmates with nearby seats.

But at this point, there was no use worrying about it. I listed a tourist spot that came to mind.

``Have you ever been to Hachimangu Shrine?''

``I have! Just once, during cherry blossom season. But it was so crowded then, I could only see people's backs. I was just thinking I wanted to take another look properly, at a slower pace.''

``Then\dots\ let's go to Hachimangu Shrine.''

After I said it, my eyes drifted to Iwama on their own. Since she was facing the ticket gates, I could see her profile now. A ponytail tied high on her head.

Sure enough, there was a cherry blossom blooming there.

``Rei!''

``Rio, good work.''

Hearing their exchange, I snapped back to myself.

There was absolutely no way that was true, but given the situation, it ended up looking like I was staring at Iwama in a daze. And before I knew it, Kannabi Rei---dressed head to toe in black---was staring intently at me.

As she took off her black wireless headphones and hung them around her neck, she greeted us.

``\dots Was I in the way?''

She really was saying the same kind of thing Mizasaki would.

Since it was right around lunchtime, we decided to eat first.

After Iwama showed up, I'd had a bad feeling---and as it turned out, Mizasaki hadn't been invited in the first place.

``Today, Rei and I were planning to sightsee around Tsunanagai together, but neither of us is from here, so we figured we should take this chance to have a local show us around.''

And for some reason, Kannabi had decided to call me. Kannabi wasn't exactly lying, but she'd invited me without telling me the crucial information that Iwama would be there. I'd fallen for her scheme completely, mistaken it for a Biology Club get-together, and ended up being dragged into an outing of two girls and one guy.

Mizasaki lived nearby too, and I could even call him over right now, but if I contacted him at this point, I could already see the future: he'd tease me with, ``Honestly, Delta, you can't even talk properly to girls unless I'm there!'' and then refuse with, ``It'd be bad of me to get in the way of you having two beauties with you.''

Like with the cherry blossom incident, I decided I was going to get through today peacefully by my own power, no matter what.

``There's an udon place I recommend. If you don't have any allergies, how about there?''

``Udon! Sounds good!''

At Iwama's reaction, Kannabi nodded too.

``I was just thinking I wanted to eat a lethal amount of wheat.''

As if.

I'd only spoken with Kannabi for the first time yesterday, and I still hadn't gotten a handle on what she was like, but somehow, being with Iwama seemed to boost her social skills. The conversation flowed well enough. Even so, I still had no idea what she was thinking. I also didn't know why I alone had been called in as the guide.

As we walked toward the udon place, I decided to listen in on the two girls' conversation for a while.

``Rei, you always get off at the next station, right? Do you live close by too?''

``Yeah. The next town over---Sunamizu Town. But I'm the ultimate indoor type, so I actually haven't come over here much.''

``Ultimate indoor type'' was a pretty distinctive turn of phrase.

Kannabi was talking perfectly normally with Iwama. I'd seen them talking in the classroom too, and if they were going out together on a day off like this, they had to be fairly close.

Kannabi, who had that unapproachable aura around her, and Iwama the class rep. They were total opposites, but maybe they had some hobby in common. Or---was it simply that Iwama was looking after Kannabi, who didn't seem like she'd be able to make friends at all?

``Rio, what area do you live in?''

``I'm from Ebiwakagawa. It's close, but also kind of far---and I didn't really come here much until middle school, either.''

Ebiwakagawa City was the most urban place in this whole area. Ebiwakagawa Station was the eastern terminus of the line that ran through Tsunanagai, and there were several large commercial complexes lined up in front of it. When Tsunanagai residents wanted to buy something big, they sometimes took the thirty-minute trip out to Ebiwakagawa.

Learning that Iwama wasn't a student from outside the prefecture, I felt relieved inside.

``I've always thought this, but isn't `Ebiwakagawa' a weird place name?''

Kannabi suddenly said something like that.

``Is it the sea or the river? Is it old or young? I'd like it to make up its mind.''

I wondered how Iwama would react to someone calling the name of her hometown weird, but---

``Right? I've been wondering about that forever!''

---she agreed with full enthusiasm.

``So I looked up the city history at the library, and it had a section on where the name came from. There's apparently a theory that it used to be a river called Wakagawa, but they renamed it to distinguish it from the nearby Akagawa. Wakagawa had a lot of freshwater prawns, and it seems like they were a local specialty. When I actually checked, you can still catch a lot of them down by the river mouth, like in the gaps between the tetrapods---''

Halfway through, Iwama abruptly fell silent, as if she'd realized something, and Kannabi spoke.

``That's interesting. Maybe next time we should go look for prawns in Ebiwaka.''

Iwama smiled happily.

``I'll help! If you're going to fish for them, bait like fish sausage works fine too---''

Until we reached the udon place, the conversation blossomed into a full discussion of how to catch freshwater prawns.

Apparently, if you caught some Ebiwaka prawns, it was good to deep-fry them plain.

After heading north from the station for a while, there was a central shopping street that ran parallel to the coastline. This one felt more geared toward tourists than the station-front shopping district, and the crowd was younger too.

The udon shop tucked away in an alley there---``Jinroku''---had the air of a hidden gem. That said, the ``hidden'' part was only in the vibe; it was often featured in guidebooks, so it was always crowded.

The table seats were full, but we were able to sit side by side---three in a row---at the counter.

From the back of the shop, it was me, then Iwama, then Kannabi. Across the counter, I could see a middle-aged man who looked like the owner, efficiently plating dishes. Deeper in the kitchen, boiling water was vigorously throwing up steam.

``This place is known for thick, chewy handmade noodles. It's easiest to tell with chilled noodles, and the chilled meat-miso udon is the standard here.''

At my explanation, Iwama and Kannabi nodded like they understood. Iwama and I ordered the chilled meat-miso udon, while Kannabi ordered curry udon.

``The scent of spices just\dots\ led me to it.''

Kannabi said it as if offering an excuse.

``When you go to an udon place or a soba place, sometimes you suddenly smell curry, right? Even if it seems delicious, if you're in the mood for Japanese food, you can't bring yourself to order that instead. But this time, since Delta brought me here, I didn't have to suffer that dilemma. Thank you.''

It was true that I'd smelled curry and thought curry udon sounded good before, but I'd never actually ordered it. I couldn't tell if I understood her or not, but I did understand that this strange classmate of mine was surprisingly logical about her own decisions. And she was more talkative than I'd expected. I also felt like she'd casually started calling me Delta, but I decided not to worry about the small stuff.

``That's good, then.''

I gave a safe response for now.

The smell of curry grew stronger. On the other side of the counter, roux had been poured into a bowl. When dashi was added on top of that, warm steam carrying both Japanese aromatics and the bite of spices drifted over. Just like Kannabi had said, it was the kind of smell that made you think, Yeah, I want that. But when I thought about the flavor of the chilled meat-miso udon, it felt like a trivial temptation.

Hot noodles went into the curry udon bowl, while noodles tightened in water were arranged into the chilled meat-miso udon bowls. With quick, practiced movements, the owner topped them with pork from a plastic container. Mizuna, chopped carrots, wakame.

``All right, thank you for waiting!''

All three bowls of udon were finished at the same time, set on a tray, and presented in front of us. The moment I received mine, a heavy weight settled into my arms.

``Whoa, it looks so good!''

Iwama let out a small cheer.

The thick white noodles---about as wide as my fingers---were rugged in that unmistakably handmade way, and they poked out here and there from the lightly filled sesame-miso soup like tree roots. The pale green of the mizuna, the orange of the carrots, and the deep green of the wakame vividly stirred my appetite.

``Let's eat.''

The three of us put our hands together.

I started by sprinkling the sliced green onions from the side dish over my udon, then mixed the ginger in with the pork. The key was not to dissolve it into the soup from the start, but to let the ginger gradually spread as you ate.

First bite.

At this shop, you couldn't slurp the noodles. Not because of manners---physically, it was difficult. The ultimate thick noodles were enough to tire your fingers just from lifting them with chopsticks. When you put them in your mouth, their springiness always surprised you. These weren't noodles you slurped---they were noodles you slowly chewed down.

When I stuffed my mouth with noodles, the sweet miso-dashi---rounded with sesame---stimulated my appetite through both taste buds and the olfactory epithelium. Each time I worked my jaw, the aroma of wheat followed just as strongly.

``Mmm---mm!''

From the intonation, it was obvious Iwama meant \textit{Delicious!} She squeezed her eyes shut, and even her expression alone made the meaning clear. After slowly chewing the noodles, she finally opened her mouth again.

``It's delicious! I've never had this flavor or texture before!''

``Yeah, you don't really get it anywhere else.''

Iwama and I both went for our second bite. Kannabi was blowing hard, doing her best to cool her noodles.

On the second bite, I mixed in the pork. The pork belly had been boiled and then chilled once, and its fat melted smoothly in my mouth, spreading sweetness. The ginger aroma supported it. There was no way that wouldn't go with the miso-dashi.

When I looked over, Kannabi was still blowing on her noodles and hadn't taken her first bite.

``What?''

Maybe she noticed my gaze---Kannabi's black eyes turned toward me with a sharp look.

``Are you bad with hot food?''

``Curry udon is different from other udon. The soup has higher viscosity, so it doesn't cool easily. It doesn't evaporate as readily, so it's less likely to lose heat through evaporation, and convection is less likely to occur, so heat transfer is less likely too.''

The oddly logical way she explained it made me like her a little more.

``Fair point. Take your time.''

Without needing me to tell her, Kannabi resumed blowing on it.

While that was happening, Iwama took another bite, then seemed to grow interested in the side dish on the tray.

``Huh, is this maybe\dots?''

As she said it, she lifted the small plate. It was a little dish of greens that came as a service.

All three of our trays had the same thing. Moist green leaves and white stems were neatly piled, but if you looked closely, bluish-purple petals were mixed in. Mountain greens, maybe. It had been squeezed, so I couldn't tell the leaf shape, and I couldn't identify it right away.

``That's katakuri ohitashi.''

The owner, apparently watching Iwama, told her with a friendly smile.

Hearing ``katakuri,'' a memory of a plastic shopping bag surfaced in my mind whether I wanted it to or not, and I fought to shake it away. Meanwhile, Iwama's eyes were shining.

``I knew it! There were flowers in it, so I thought maybe. You can eat parts other than the underground stem, too.''

``Yes. You can eat everything, from the flowers to the roots. Though if you eat too much, it'll upset your stomach.''
