As expected---she probably knew a lot about animal behavior. What senpai said was convincing.

But there was still something I couldn't accept about her theory.

``Senpai says one of those three took him, but did they really? One of them was scared of hamsters to begin with. Another was told that lie that Jounouchi bites, so he wouldn't have felt like touching him. And the one who fell hurt both hands.''

``\dots''

Senpai didn't argue back. I continued.

``When the three of them left the biology room, I was watching. None of them looked like they were carrying Jounouchi, and there wasn't any sign of him escaping at their feet, either. Jounouchi fell off the desk for some reason, and it's still in this biology room. Let's split up and search.''

She couldn't argue with that, either. Senpai closed her eyes for a moment like she was reflecting, then said---

``\dots You're right. Let's do that. It's not like I'm blaming you guys\dots\ sorryyy.''

She lowered her gaze awkwardly, then turned her back to us.

An awkward silence, to an almost painful degree.

The four of us exchanged looks and nodded to each other---either way, we had to find Jounouchi.

Fortunately, the biology room was sealed up to prevent Rotgelb from escaping. The door the three had left through was locked immediately so it couldn't be opened from outside. The door leading to the biology prep room was locked too, and the prep room was empty, so it wouldn't be opened from that side. According to Karato-senpai, the biology room didn't even have small gaps---so that insects and small animals couldn't get in from outside.

In other words, this space was currently a closed room with no way for a hamster to escape, and unless Jounouchi had pulled off some elaborate trick, we could assume he was still somewhere inside the biology room.

We split up and began searching the biology room.

When it comes to the long table where Jounouchi had been, we left it as-is to preserve the scene. On top of the long table were only the cage and the maze. We'd already confirmed that Jounouchi wasn't hidden in either of them. We started searching from around the table and, just in case, each of us checked inside our own bags too, then gradually expanded the search area.

I moved toward the back of the biology room. It was cluttered with assorted junk, and there were plenty of places a hamster could hide. For now, I observed the nearest cabinet.

``Wait.''

Senpai's voice came from behind me. I turned around.

``I'll search there. You should go talk to those three after all. Just in case.''

``\dots I'm sorry, but I don't think those three kidnapped Jounouchi.''

``Then explain how Jounouchi disappeared from on top of the desk.''

I was at a loss for words. In a sense, the top of the desk was closed as well. To a hamster, the surroundings were sheer cliffs. She said it had never once fallen off the edge.

``No\dots\ that's not it. Sorryyy.''

When I stayed silent, Karato-senpai apologized.

``I'm going to the restroom. After I leave, lock up, and keep searching.''

And then she hurried out of the biology room---running, but being careful only when she opened the door.

``Okay\dots\ what do we do?''

As Mizasaki said that, Iwama put a hand on the entrance door.

``For now, I'll lock it.''

Clack. With that, the biology room was closed again. Jounouchi should be in here somewhere.

Looking at the biology room---which, to a hamster, was about the size of a small isolated island---I let out a sigh.

``\dots We've got no choice but to keep searching the hard way.''

``Yeah.''

Staring down at the old plank floor, we searched in silence for a while. They'd probably done a big cleanup at the end of the school year---there was almost no trash, and maybe it had been waxed, because our indoor shoes squeaked against it. Jounouchi had eaten a fair bit earlier. Maybe it had dropped one or two droppings.

``\dots Jounouchi-kun, why did you disappear from the top of the desk?''

After a while, Iwama muttered. Kannabi lifted her face.

``Strange. Like a kamikakushi.''

``Same as you and Delta, I don't think those three are involved either. They're awful, but still.''

For some reason, I went back to the cabinet at the back of the classroom.

``I don't know if it's related, but\dots\ didn't senpai seem a little strange earlier?''

At my remark, Mizasaki nodded.

``Yeah. Like she was hiding something shady around there.''

When I tried to search this area, she'd suddenly stopped me. There might be some secret here, connected to Jounouchi's disappearance\dots\ probably unlikely, but checking was free. I opened the cabinet drawers from the bottom up, one by one.

This should have been the cabinet where Karato-senpai had searched for the animal-care manual and pulled out one sheet. But remarkably, every drawer was empty.

``\dots Find anything?''

Iwama had come over beside me.

Shaking my head, I took a single ring binder out of the top drawer I'd opened last.

``This is all that was in the cabinet.''

``Hm\dots? An album?''

I handed it to Iwama. When she opened the thick binder, it was filled with tons of photos.

``Yeah. The one last year's graduates made, right? Tokumura-sensei showed it to me.''

Mizasaki and Kannabi leaned in too. Iwama awkwardly turned the thick pages. It recorded what the Biology Club had looked like back when it wasn't down to a single member.

``There aren't many members, but\dots\ they look like they're having so much fun.''

Looking at a photo of club members laughing around Rotgelb, Kannabi said---

We're welcoming Roo-chan as a new member. Even when summer vacation starts, may Roo-chan not get lonely!

It had been taken about a year ago, right after Golden Week. On the next page was a group photo taken in the biology room before summer vacation, with a note that the third-years were retiring.

I'd heard that at this school, a lot of third-years start focusing on entrance exam study around the start of summer vacation. At the latest, they retire once the September cultural festival ends. Last year, in the Biology Club, the seniors retired without even waiting for the end of summer.

So for about eight months after that, had Karato-senpai been taking care of the animals all by herself?

``Samishii-nee\dots''

From the cage stored at the back of the classroom, Rotgelb's voice reached us.

In an instant, my skin prickled.

Her mutters were something I'd been casually ignoring up until now.

But unless someone had said ``How lonely,'' there was no way a budgerigar would say that.

Rotgelb had arrived last May. The third-years retired in July.

Karato-senpai had been left behind all alone, talking to the budgerigar---

The album trembled faintly. It was Iwama's hands holding it that were shaking.

``Keeping a club going by yourself\dots\ that must've been hard\dots''

After saying that, Iwama snapped back to herself, shut the album, and put it back in the drawer.

``We have to look for Jounouchi-kun.''

I'd been completely distracted by the album too. I still didn't really understand why senpai had tried to hide this cabinet, but at the very least, it didn't seem to have anything to do with the Jounouchi disappearance incident.

More importantly, given what an animal-loving senpai she was, if it were something that even might relate to Jounouchi going missing, she wouldn't hide it from us.

\dots Huh?

I pulled the album out again. Maybe because the thickness of the pages was uneven, it flipped open right to the page I'd been about to look at.

Jounouchi kept running. Was he turning the play equipment, or was the play equipment making him run?

It was a photo of a hamster playing on an exercise wheel---peaceful, ordinary.

But it gave me a flash of insight.

I looked at the long table where Jounouchi had vanished. The cage, the maze, and---

Something was missing!

``Mizasaki---where's the duct tape?''

Leaving the album in the open drawer, I rushed over to the long table.

``Huh? Duct tape?''

``That duct tape that was basically trash---what senpai gave you. You took it and put it on the desk, didn't you?''

``Now that you mention it, it's gone\dots\ Wait---ah! So that's what it is!''

``What is it?''

At Kannabi's question, Mizasaki twisted his face with obvious regret.

``Sorry! This is all my fault. When I put the duct tape on the desk where Jounouchi was, I didn't set it flat---I set it down on the side of the roll. Like an exercise wheel.''

I remembered Mizasaki's eyes looking at me through the hole in the roll.

Iwama let out a small gasp.

``Jounouchi-kun climbed inside, and with no idea where he was going, he kept moving forward and fell with the duct tape.''

I nodded.

``Yeah. An exercise wheel stays in one place, but duct tape doesn't.''

``Then where is the duct tape? I looked at the floor, but it wasn't there.''

Kannabi seemed to notice something and walked over to the trash can. She picked up the tape core.

``This\dots\ the black-haired one from those three---''

With that, I remembered when we'd been cleaning up the glass shards.

``\dots Right. Fujito used the tape that had fallen to pick up the tiny glass fragments.''

The three of us gathered around Kannabi. The core was pretty old---and it was used up. Almost certainly, it was the same one Mizasaki had set down on the desk with Jounouchi.

``Do you think there's any clue here? Should we ask Fujito-kun where it fell? Maybe call him?''

``Yeah. We can call and---''

``Wait. This.''

Kannabi cut me off.

Was she seriously saying there was a clue to Jounouchi's whereabouts on a duct tape core?

``\dots There's a little blood on it, I think.''

Kannabi indicated part of the core. On the brown cardboard, there was a faint dark red smear, like it had been grazed.

``Are you sure it's blood? It might just be an ink stain that was already there.''

``Let's check!''

Iwama immediately pulled out a pocket tissue and lightly rubbed the dark red spot.

A faint red transferred onto the white tissue. I see. Probably fresh blood.

For a moment, we were all at a loss for words. Had Jounouchi been injured when he fell? It was only a tiny amount of bleeding, so maybe it wasn't a serious injury, but\dots\ we needed to find him quickly.

Iwama thought with a serious look.

``But\dots\ if Jounouchi-kun really is hurt, then maybe we can follow the blood, right?''

``No, Gamma-san. On this floor, it'd be hard. A hamster's tiny bleeding and all.''

I looked down at the floor. The faint hope that had started to swell deflated immediately. Dark brown flooring with black grain. Even if there was a little blood on it, we'd never be able to see it.

``Not with our eyes, probably. But\dots\ scientifically!''

Scientifically---was that even possible?

``If we have some kind of reagent, we could trace the blood. For example, the luminol reaction is used in forensic investigations, and it can detect even tiny amounts of blood.''

``The problem is whether this school even has that kind of chemical,''

Kannabi pointed out, but Mizasaki and I couldn't help exchanging looks.

Normally, Iwama's comment would've ended as nothing more than an outlandish idea.

But one way or another, this was Tsunanagai High School.

Right after Mizasaki dashed out of the biology room, heavy footsteps thudded from upstairs. Don't run in the hallway.

Since he'd left without saying anything, Iwama and Kannabi were still sitting there, dumbfounded.

``Let's close the curtains.''

That was all I said. Mizasaki would be back soon.

Sure enough, just as I finished closing them, there was a knock at the door, and Mizasaki's voice said, ``Open up.''

After confirming Jounouchi wasn't at our feet, I let Mizasaki in.

``As expected of you, Gamma-san. That idea was way too good.''

Breathing hard, Mizasaki showed Iwama a small silver pouch.

``That is\dots?''

Mizasaki pulled a spray bottle out of the pouch---the luminol reaction luminescent reagent we'd failed to get at last week's club fair. It was what Hongo-senpai had made an excess of and never used. Luckily, there was still some left.

``No way\dots\ luminol?''

``Yeah. I got it from the Chemistry Club.''

As if he couldn't even spare the time to finish talking, he strode over to the long table where Jounouchi had been. If the duct tape had rolled off, it should be near Mizasaki's chair. He dropped to one knee and flashed me an OK sign.

``Alright. Lights out.''

I turned off the lights. The only illumination now was a faint sliver of natural light leaking through the curtains. With this, we wouldn't miss even a weak glow on the floor.

``It should be basic and have hydrogen peroxide dissolved in it. If it gets in your eyes, it's dangerous, so stand back a bit.''

As he spoke, Mizasaki sprayed the luminescent reagent onto the floor.

First spray. Nothing appeared.

Second spray. Still nothing. Was the reagent too old?

``\dots What are you doing?''

To Kannabi's question, I answered.

``If there's blood, no matter how tiny the amount, this reagent will make it glow. The floor was just waxed at the end of the school year. If Jounouchi injured his foot and bled, only those footprints will light up.''

How many sprays had it been? Still on one knee, Mizasaki kept spraying with an intensity I'd never seen from him.

``Woooah!''

At Mizasaki's shout, I crept closer and peered down. On the pitch-black floor, there were pale bluish dots of light. And they weren't random---at nearly even intervals, they formed a line.

``Yes! It lit up!''

I couldn't help blurting it out too.

``Amazing\dots\ it's like forensic science.''

Iwama was completely absorbed, staring at the glowing floor close enough that her shoulder brushed mine.

In the dark biology room, the light, crisp sound of Mizasaki's spray echoed. In the darkness spreading at our feet, more footprints began to flicker into view.

I could feel myself being drawn in by that faint light.

Our chemistry knowledge---actually helping solve a real problem, right in front of us.

This was scientific, in the truest sense.

The reason the cherry blossom heart had been broken. The reason the ginkgo's age had been hidden. Iwama had started to teach me the unexpected fun that comes from examining the strange things around us scientifically.

For someone like me, who'd lived in a narrow world, it was nothing short of a Copernican revolution.

Up until now, I think I'd put some kind of partition between studying science and living my everyday life. But science isn't only for scientists.

You can use it to resolve questions, and you can use it to achieve your goals.

So this is what it means to look out over the city you live in from the shoulders of giants.

The spray sounded in intermittent bursts.

The glowing footprints continued all the way beneath the sink by the window. There was a small cabinet there, with one section slightly ajar. Mizasaki signaled to me in front of it. I went to the biology room entrance and turned the lights back on.

With Iwama and Kannabi watching, Mizasaki slowly opened the cabinet.

``Wah---yes!''

\fullpageimage[angle = 90]{6.jpg}


\thispagestyle{plain}

\vspace{1cm}

Iwama clapped. A victory for science. Kannabi's eyes widened, and for once she showed a genuinely happy smile.

On Mizasaki's upturned hand as he stood, Jounouchi was perched neatly in place.

Karato-senpai came back a little later, out of breath, while we were cleaning the floor.

It had taken far too long for a bathroom break, and if she'd used the restroom nearby, there'd have been no need to run. It seemed likely she'd chased after the Ototo Trio as witnesses and gone to ask them questions, unwilling to waste time trying to persuade me. But since senpai didn't bring it up, I chose not to touch the topic either.

When we told her Jounouchi had been found, senpai's eyes welled up as she rejoiced, repeating, ``Thank you, thank you so much,'' over and over. Even when we told her about the duct tape and the injury, she didn't get angry.

``I'm just glad you found him. That's all that matters. Thank you so, so much.''

In the end, tears even spilled from the corners of her eyes.

Karato-senpai's family runs an animal hospital. She called Tokumura-sensei and told him she'd be taking Jounouchi home today. From the look of it, the injury wasn't that serious. Still, for a while, he'd have to focus on recuperating. The maze would have to wait.

The 5 p.m. departure time was approaching.

When we were about to head home, senpai noticed that a cabinet drawer had been left open. The album was there, still open.

``Ahh, embarrassing.''

Saying that, senpai closed the album with a gentle touch.

``I end up looking at it sometimes. Even though I'm supposed to have no interest in humans.''

She slowly slid the drawer shut.

``Roo-chan, ohayo!''

``Yeah, yeah---Roo-chan, ohayo!''

Even though it was already evening, Karato-senpai replied to the budgerigar like that.

``The senpai used to call both me and Rotgelb `Roo-chan,' you know. So even now, we still call each other Roo-chan.''

As if to hide her embarrassment, she said that, then muttered---

``Come to think of it, there are four of you. No way that's a coincidence\dots\ honestly, that guy\dots''

``\dots What do you mean?''

At Mizasaki's question, Karato-senpai shook her head.

``No, it's nothing. By the way, there wasn't some paper tucked into the album, was there?''

``Paper? Gamma-san, what was it again?''

``No, I didn't see anything in particular\dots\ Senpai, are you looking for something?''

``No. If not, it's fine. Next activity is the day after tomorrow. I need to go to the staff room once to get the key for this place, so you can all head home first.''

And then she added---

``Welcome to the Biology Club, you young birds.''

When I hurried back to the shoe lockers, only Iwama was waiting for me.

``Huh? Where are Mizasaki and Kannabi?''

``They said they had something urgent, so they both went home first.''

``In the last few minutes? What could possibly be so urgent?''

``Who knows.''

After tilting her head slightly, Iwama added as if she'd just remembered.

``Rei said to tell Del-chan `bye-bye.'''

That little---

Kannabi's comment could only be provocation, and there was no way Mizasaki had anything urgent to do. It was a scheme to make me and Iwama walk home alone together. In that sense, those two were on the same wavelength. In fact, between the cherry blossoms and what happened on Saturday, they'd already pulled the same kind of thing more than once.

I'm never telling you the truth.

Yeah---the truth.

We were about to leave the biology room together as a group of four, but there was something I couldn't stop thinking about, so I went back alone to confirm it.

There was only one question.

Was what senpai wanted to hide really the album?

``If it was the album, I don't think it was something she needed to hide in the first place.''

That had been Mizasaki's point.

``Delta was searching for Jounouchi. Just because he came near the cabinet, there's no reason to stop him. If she didn't want the album's contents seen, she should've just left it alone. By stopping him, she basically made sure the album got opened anyway.''

In other words, he thought something even more suspicious had been hidden there.

``And asking whether there was paper tucked inside\dots\ even if it was embarrassment, that question felt weird.''

Kannabi had been thinking the same thing. She was right---what a strange thing to ask.

And that's when it hit me.

It had to be hidden there---in that spot---

I told the three of them to wait at the shoe lockers, and while senpai went to the staff room to get the key, I checked the actual thing in the biology room. Just as I'd thought, it was hidden exactly where I expected.

And when I came back, Mizasaki and Kannabi---who were supposed to be waiting---were gone.

With no other choice, I ended up walking home with just Iwama.

We went down the slope lined with ginkgo trees. The leaves were much fuller now than when we'd gone to see the cherry blossoms.

Iwama fell into step right beside me. She was close. Even when I tried to glance at her profile, the sun hanging in the western sky was too dazzling.

``\dots Did you find it? The thing Karato-senpai was trying to hide.''

At Iwama's question, I nodded.

While I was hesitating over whether I should say it out loud, Iwama spoke first.

``I think it was the care manual.''

So she already knew. Then there was no point hiding it. I nodded again.

``Yeah. The clear pockets in the ring binder the album used---meant for storing documents---were A4 size. The drawing paper kept in them was A4 too. The side without photos was pressed back-to-back, and in the gap between them, the B5 care manual was hidden.''

It was a paper stash.

The moment I confirmed it existed, I left the biology room, so I didn't know how many pages there were. But there had been quite a lot of them hidden in the album's pockets.

``I thought that album was hard to flip through,''

Iwama said with a faint smile.

That's right. The first time I saw that album was when Mizasaki and I went to the biology room with Mikage Aya. Tokumura-sensei had handed it to us. Mizasaki had flipped through the pages rapidly.

But today, when Iwama opened the album we'd found in that cabinet, the pages seemed hard to turn. And when I tried to find Jounouchi's photo, the thickness of the pages was uneven.

The album's shape had changed.

Only Iwama and I---who had actually opened it today---knew what felt off about those pockets.

``You noticed from the moment you opened it?''

``\dots Yeah.''

But she hadn't told Mizasaki or Kannabi. It was something someone had been hiding---something she'd wanted to hide. It wasn't something to blab about carelessly. Still, if it was just the two of us---Iwama and me---who both knew the truth, discussing it a little wouldn't bring down any punishment.

``When I demanded the manual, senpai went over to search that cabinet. She took strangely long, and in the end she brought only a single sheet---the hamster care manual. She said that was all she could find.''

``Yeah. But I think she had it all then. She just decided to pretend she'd only found one sheet, and hide the rest.''

``That manual had `No removal' written on it. So she couldn't bring herself to put it in her bag and take it home. She needed a place she could hide it on the spot, inside the biology room.''

Karato-senpai tried, out of a sense of duty, to follow the rules that her own senpai had written into the manual.

``Right. So she chose the album. If she hid it between the pockets, she probably figured it wouldn't be found unless something pretty extreme happened.''

But senpai had made a mistake. Afraid the manual would be discovered, she'd tried to pull me away from the cabinet. That only made us suspicious. A blunder born of sincerity. And asking, ``There wasn't paper tucked into the album, was there?'' when she learned we'd found the album---probably a precautionary check to see whether we'd noticed her paper stash---had only backfired.

The real question was why.

``But\dots\ why would she do that\dots?''

She could've just handed everything over. There was nothing incriminating written in it. Senpai shouldn't have had any reason to hide the care manual.

From the side, Iwama leaned in and peered at me, looking oddly amused.

``This is just my imagination, so hear me out, okay?''

Walking slowly, Iwama continued.

``If she'd handed us not just the hamster manual, but the care manuals for the other animals too\dots\ maybe she thought it would feel like she was dumping everything on us.''

``\dots Ah. I see.''

We were brand-new members. And it was our first day of real activity. Even if she needed to teach us how to care for them, she probably felt awkward about handing over care manuals for every living thing right away. But since the conversation had been moving toward giving us everything, she needed an excuse not to. So she hid the rest.

It was her own clumsy kindness---trying not to let us notice she was being considerate.

Iwama kept going.

``Delta, do you remember? The hamster manual had the date it was written.''

``I think it was April of\dots\ 2020.''

``Yeah. April.''

Four years ago. We'd only just started sixth grade. But I remembered that time clearly.

The month the state of emergency had been declared.

Around then, the way schools and clubs worked changed drastically. In March, school closures were announced, and before I knew it, the new school year had started. And then---April.

Iwama must've had a reason for bringing up that period. I waited for what she'd say next.

``I think it was a guidebook that the second- and third-years back then put together desperately. Just like Del-chan's friend said, even if activities were restricted, they still had to keep taking care of the animals. But it wasn't easy for the upperclassmen to coach the underclassmen closely. So that heavily annotated guidebook came to exist.''

So that was it.

A guidebook that was that detailed wouldn't really come about in normal club activities where you could just pass things down by word of mouth.

``So it wasn't a very good situation to begin with, huh.''

``I think that's how Karato-senpai saw it. From the moment senpai first received those papers.''

Since I'm not Mikage Aya, I tried folding my fingers and counting quietly. Karato-senpai enrolled at Tsunanagai High School in April 2022. The third-years at the time were the first-years from when the guidebook was created.

Once I actually counted it out, I realized just how intense the turnover in a club really was.

Every April, anyone who knew what things were like more than two years ago was gone.

By the time Karato-senpai joined the club, the students who'd experienced activities before the restrictions were already gone. All of her upperclassmen were students who had somehow managed to keep the animals' care going while operating under restrictions.

A lot of what made the activities appealing had probably been lost quickly. The fact that there were no other third-years besides Karato-senpai---and not a single second-year---told that story vividly.

Unlike the Physics Club or the Chemistry Club, the Biology Club hadn't made it through that rough sea unscathed.

And the care guidebook that had been left behind in the middle of it all had four years' worth of bleakness soaked into it.

For Karato-senpai, maybe it even felt like a symbol of the Biology Club's decline.

``That's why, you know, I think the reason senpai didn't give us the guidebook was, in a way, a declaration of resolve. Like---now that first-years finally came in, she was declaring that she wouldn't let the same thing happen again.''

Was that really so? Had Karato-senpai actually thought that far?

Well, just like Iwama had said, this was an extension of ``delusion.''

``Could be.''

That was all I decided to say. Even if it was wrong, nobody lost anything.

We came out onto the central shopping street, lively with evening shoppers. Before I knew it, I'd missed the turnoff toward my house. Dragged along by Iwama, I was walking pointlessly toward the station. It felt awkward to announce, this late, that I'd only just noticed. If I was going to turn back anyway, maybe I should just go all the way to the station.

As I idly thought about that, Iwama said as if she were psyching herself up.

``Let's do our best!''

Her eyes caught the sunset and shone with a fierce brightness.

``I really think the Biology Club can bounce back if it's us. So---let's do our best.''

``\dots Yeah. Let's do our best.''

I felt like repeating it wasn't enough, so I added---

``Count on me.''

``Same here. Count on me.''

Even though all we were doing was trading obvious words back and forth, it somehow felt strangely ticklish.

From the exhaust vent of a small restaurant we'd just passed, the scent of broth drifted out. Man, I was getting hungry.

``Maybe the effect of those cherry blossoms is starting to kick in.''

Because Iwama suddenly said something like that, I messed up my breathing and ended up choking badly on my own saliva. I turned my face away and bent forward at the waist.

``Ah! Sorry---I didn't mean it in a weird way\dots\ You know, like---having a lucky high school life, and we made that wish on the Inome, right? That kind of meaning. Yeah.''

``It's fine. I know.''

``I see\dots\ but you were choking really hard.''

``No need to worry. It happens fairly often.''

``Want to use a handkerchief?''

I shook my head and pulled out a pocket tissue. Finally, my airway and diaphragm started to settle down. Iwama watched me for a while, then eventually opened her mouth, as if choosing her words.

``\dots But really, it's kind of like a miracle, isn't it?''

``A miracle?''

I thought it was a pretty unscientific thing to say, but Iwama looked completely undoubtful about it.

``Yeah---a miracle. Because of that whole cherry-blossom incident, I got to learn that there are people like you, Del-chan---people I can call comrades. And because you learned that I admire people like that, Rei gave me that push from behind\dots\ and that made me think it's okay for me to go down this path. It feels like I finally made a decision for my own sake---by myself.''

I see, I said, nodding.

Iwama had been torn. Whether to become the version of herself that others wanted, or to walk the road she wanted to take.

Maybe seeing those cherry blossoms had been a distant cause that led Iwama to choose the latter.

That familiar ``Did you see that smile?'' was turned toward me.

``Because we saw that `happy cherry blossom' together, I really think that might be why I'm who I am now.''

After seeing Iwama off at the station and heading back home, I found myself thinking back over what had happened since I enrolled.

It felt like I'd solved an awful lot of mysteries.

Together with Iwama, I'd solved the mystery of the Kanshoudai and discovered a cherry-blossom shape just like the legend said.

I'd solved the mystery behind the club recruitment scheme Mikage set up, and decided to join the Biology Club together with Mizasaki.

Invited by Kannabi, I'd solved the mystery of the ginkgo, and in the process, ended up inviting Iwama to join the Biology Club too.

And today, at long last, club activities began---and the four of us worked together to solve the mystery of Jounouchi's disappearance.

It had been a start full of mysteries, but it was that perfect accumulation of them that led to where we were now.

A lucky high school life---those cherry blossoms on the back mountain might really have granted our wish.

This year, the shape of happiness that only Iwama and I found.

A pale pink Inome that nobody else could find.

\dots Huh?

Something caught at the edge of my mind. It was only a slight sense of wrongness, but it was clearly off.

The day we saw the Inome---why had those words come out of her mouth\dots?

Once I started doubting, I began noticing other physical evidence that strongly suggested that person's involvement.

That equation, too. The posters, too.

And then---ah. So that's what that was---

Like a snowball rolling downhill, the suspicion swelled and grew.

I could write it all off as the cherry blossoms' magic. Because we saw the Inome in the cherry blossoms, we got to have a lucky start to our high school lives. But was it really okay to leave it at that?

The cherry-blossom incident was set up by Mizasaki. The trial-club thing was set up by Mikage. The Saturday outing was set up by Kannabi.

Even though they were three people who shouldn't have had any connection to begin with, each of their actions had contributed to the four of us ending up together as new members of the Biology Club.

Just like Iwama said---like a miracle.

But if it wasn't just a miracle\dots?

It probably wasn't that she'd sensed what was going on in my head, but after I crossed the crosswalk, I noticed a girl waiting for me. When our eyes met, she gave a small bow.

``Got a minute?''

In a low, clear voice that gave nothing away.

``\dots There's something I want to talk to you about, Delta-kun.''

It was Mikage Aya.

% ==============================
%        Fragment
% ==============================
\clearpage
\thispagestyle{plain}
\phantomsection
\begin{center}
    \large\bfseries
    Fragment\\
    \textit{Erythronium japonicum}
\end{center}
\label{sec:fragment2}
\addcontentsline{toc}{chapter}{Fragment}
\vspace{1cm}

``When it comes to Rio---why are you always so high-and-mighty?''

When she said it to me for the first time, what came over me wasn't so much shock as it was relief.

At last, she'd said what she really thought. The reason those girls had come to hate me and ignore me wasn't because I'd done something decisively unforgivable.

It wasn't because I'd pushed ahead with a vegetation survey even though the weather was bad and it was only drizzling, and it wasn't because I'd tried to increase our activities beyond twice a week, and it wasn't because I'd turned down a sudden confession from the boy Sana liked---

It was simply because I was acting high-and-mighty.

I had considered that possibility myself.

Of course, it wasn't like I'd been puffing out my chest and saying, ``I'm important.'' Studying hard for high school entrance exams. Taking on the role of class representative even though no one else wanted to. Running for student council president because a teacher recommended it. Volunteering to be club president to try to liven up the Science Club. The accumulation of those things had made me look ``high-and-mighty.'' But that was how I lived my life.

``You're always talking about weird stuff. It's honestly exhausting---talking to you, Rio.''

Sana even said that to me. That was why they'd started ignoring me, she said.

I'd talked science endlessly with my fellow Science Club members. I thought it was fun, but apparently they didn't. I might have thought I was just chatting about topics I liked, but in reality, I might have been one-sidedly showering them with knowledge---acting superior.

It was simply sad that I'd lost my friends because of the very thing I thought was fun.

Even though I was club president, I couldn't go to the club anymore.

``You're just bad at living, you know. Even though your specs are so high.''

Yuka held up both hands and made a wide rectangular ``screen,'' framing my face inside it.

It was lunchtime behind the middle school building, just the two of us. I swallowed the rice I'd been chewing for no reason at all.

``Am I\dots?''

Yuka was the only one I was close enough with that I didn't need to wedge in a modest ``That's not true.'' Yuka knew me well. She was much cuter than I was, had outstanding athletic ability, and her grades were about the same as mine. We were the same year, but she was like a senior in life. I could always accept Yuka's compliments honestly.

``You pick way too many low-cost-performance options. I'm not saying it's pointless, but you're going out of your way to take the hard road. Class rep, student council president---if it's your grades, Rio, you shouldn't need to care about internal assessment points at all. Same with the Science Club. Even if you work hard there, all you get is bonus `weirdo points.'''

``I see.''

I took it in once, then said---

``But the Science Club is different. I don't think it's hard. It's something I do because I like it. You like basketball too, right, Yuka? It's the same thing.''

The cost-performance might be bad, and maybe what it ``earns'' isn't popularity points---but when you're trying to do what you like, profit-and-loss calculations shouldn't matter.

``Sticking to what you like is a good thing, of course. But you also have the option of not putting it out front. Do you really need to cling to the Science Club? It's a club full of nothing but introverts. You don't have to try so hard there, Rio. Even back in elementary school, you did your research all by yourself, didn't you?''

Yuka was a bold person, but she wasn't the type to badmouth people. The reason she was talking about the Science Club like that was because she was listening to me and helping me think through being called ``high-and-mighty'' by the other club members.

``By myself\dots\ huh.''

``Yeah. You don't have to change how you live, but do it a little more skillfully.''

In the end, I didn't need to quit the Science Club. Not long after that, I ended up being the only member anyway. In the first and second years, we were required to belong to some club, but there was no such rule for third-years. In spring, the moment we became third-years, everyone quit---boys included.

There were no underclassmen.

``Having new first-years come in is a pain, right? So we kept chasing them off.''

I heard that from Sana on graduation day.

The katakuri Del-chan gave me was crushed flat, completely dried out, its color badly faded.

Even so, every time I looked at it, that beautiful memory came back to me. Spring---the vivid pale pink that drew insects in.

But I think the true essence of katakuri is actually underground.

In the pressed-flower specimen, everything from blossom to root is there. The carefully dug-up thin bulb makes me recall the long hardship of katakuri, steadily storing starch---but only in early spring.

Eight years.

That's how long it takes for a sprouted katakuri to bloom.

I don't know how plants ``feel''---or rather, plants without nervous systems shouldn't have feelings at all---but if, hypothetically, feelings did dwell within them, then perhaps katakuri spends eight years dreaming of the day it will bloom.

The day it shyly presents the fruits of all those years endured deep underground, on spring's stage.

% ==============================
%        Chapter 5
% ==============================
\clearpage
\thispagestyle{plain}
\phantomsection
\begin{center}
    \large\bfseries
    Chapter 5\\
    To Keep Them from Killing the Little Giant
\end{center}
\label{sec:ch5}
\addcontentsline{toc}{chapter}{Chapter 5}
\vspace{1cm}

I was brought all the way to Sansetsuto. The sinking sun streamed into the shop through the wide windows.

The orange light should have been beautiful, yet it felt somehow stifling.

Like the sky itself was telling me, in the end, you can't escape this cycle.

At the very back of the shop, there was a single private room. The door across from the restroom---always kept shut. Mikage led me there.

``Go in.''

Urged to open it, I looked down at the stylish brass doorknob. If Mikage had wanted to talk with me alone, she would have opened it herself. Someone was already waiting inside this room.

After clearing my throat with a small cough, I knocked and opened the door.

At first, the harsh western sun burned my eyes. Gradually, an antique-style table and chairs came into view.

And sure enough, there was one person waiting alone---exactly who I had expected.

``Oh, you're here, Delchi. Good work---especially since it's after club. Sit, sit!''

Hongo Nagisa, the Chemistry Club President. Still in uniform, she sipped her coffee at ease.

With a four-person table between us, Mikage and I sat across from her. Through the even larger window, we could see the sea dyed in sunset colors---but my mind was not on that at all.

What kind of conversation were we about to have in this room?

``No need to be nervous. Here---what'll you order?''

She handed a menu across the table. Something about her fingers felt off. The gaudy nails were gone; her nails were neatly trimmed, painted only in a turquoise-like color. If even those flashy nails had been worn just to rack up our disgust, then all I could say was: impressive.

Sansetsuto's recommendation was still the same as always: the Spring Blend.

``I've decided.''

``What about you, Aya-chii?''

After a brief hesitation, Mikage quietly said only, ``Blend.''

``O-kay.''

I thought senpai was going to call a staff member, but instead she tilted her cup and finished it.

That was when a knock sounded.

``Excuse me.''

A young male staff member opened the door and came in. Three cups sat on a silver tray. Hongo-senpai took her cafe latte, then gestured with her hand for him to place the cherry-colored cup in front of me and the white cup in front of Mikage.

No way---I was left speechless.

We hadn't ordered yet. I hadn't even stated that I would order the Spring Blend.

And yet, the cherry-colored cup placed in front of me was unmistakably the Spring Blend, and I also knew that the coffee in the white cup placed in front of Mikage was Sansetsuto's regular blend.

It was like a magic trick. \dots\ Or what, did this senpai read my mind?

``Surprised? I'm pretty good at stuff like this, you know.''

``What exactly is this supposed to mean?''

It was both anger at what she was playing at, and the question of how she did it.

``I figured if I didn't demonstrate it, you wouldn't believe what I'm about to say. If I reveal the trick---well, Delchi would pick the recommendation without hesitation, and Aya-chii always gets a cafe latte, but today she wouldn't want to owe me anything, so she'd pick the cheapest option instead. I just predicted that. That's all.''

It was hard to believe.

Setting Mikage aside, how did she know me that well when we'd only talked a little during new member recruitment?

\dots\ No, she must have known.

Because she knew, she could manipulate us.

I didn't touch the Spring Blend. I stared straight at Hongo-senpai---the true enemy.

``Why did you call me here?''

\fullpageimage{7.jpg}


\thispagestyle{plain}

\vspace{1cm}

``Judging by that serious look on your face, it's probably exactly what you're thinking, Delchi. I figured it was about time you'd notice, so I thought I'd get ahead of it and confess.''

After noisily slurping her cafe latte as if it were hot, she looked back at me with wide-open eyes.

``Go on, go on---ask whatever you want. Big sis is gonna answer anything today.''

Mikage seemed intent on keeping silent. She probably didn't want to talk about anything. From where I sat, I could see her clenching her fist tight in her lap.

There were a lot of things I wanted to ask. But first, I should start with the very first thing that had felt off.

After taking a deep breath, I said it.

``When we went to see the cherry blossoms on the back hill, I passed you and Mikage-senpai on your way down.''

``Mm-hm, mm-hm. That's right.''

``Back then, you said this---`We went to all that trouble to climb up, and it was a letdown.'''

``And?''

``That doesn't make sense. The one who told Mizasaki that the cherry-blossom heart had collapsed was Hongo-senpai---you. If you already knew from the start that the heart wouldn't be visible this year, calling it `a letdown'---''

Senpai nodded, her smile never wavering.

``True.''

``So why did you say that?''

``I figured actually hearing the voice of someone who couldn't see it would make for a bigger impact when you did see it. You know---planting the audience, that kind of thing? Not because it's sakura, or anything---though it's not like that pun wasn't there---but if there was nobody else, I thought you two might turn back halfway. Just in case.''

She said something terrifying as if it were nothing. In other words, she'd been trying to manipulate the impressions Iwama and I formed.

``Why would you do something like that?''

``You didn't notice? That cherry tree was in full bloom, and yet nobody else came to see it, right? That's part of it too. One of the traditions that's been dying thanks to the `restrictions' of the last four years. Supposedly, up until five years ago they did upkeep on the viewing platform and pruned the tree too, but that stopped.''

I remembered. Mizasaki had said it was supposed to be a famous cherry tree, and yet the only people we'd seen that day besides Iwama and me were Hongo-senpai and Mikage-senpai. And the signboard that was supposed to be there had been covered over with lichen.

``And the platform being in the wrong place is because of that, too. When the tree fell, the teacher who handled it didn't know anything about the legend. The viewing spot matters, but instead they just moved the platform so students wouldn't have to climb over fallen wood, and called it done.''

``\dots\dots I don't really understand.''

``What don't you understand?''

``I mean---why did you egg Mizasaki on, push me into a place like that, and what exactly were you trying to do?''

Senpai lifted her eyebrows as if she were surprised. She looked at me like, \textit{You seriously don't get it?}

``Because if you and Riochi solved the cherry-blossom mystery together, you'd get closer, and you'd get to know each other better. What other reason did you think there was?''

I'd braced myself for the possibility that it was something like that, so the shock probably didn't show on my face. But Mikage---who hadn't moved at all until now---shifted her face slightly and looked at me. Was she worried about me?

``\dots\dots How much did Mizasaki know?''

``All I did was tell Mizacchi about the cherry tree. Like, `You should tell your friends, okay? Especially if you've got a guy and a girl you wanna get together---might be a good tip,' that sort of thing.''

It was true---if that was all he'd been told, Mizasaki would find it amusing and start plotting to push Iwama and me together.

But still, why did Hongo-senpai know that much about us?

``Guess I forgot to tell you the premise. My boyfriend's really well-connected, so I looked into most of the promising new students before they even enrolled. You know---profiling and all that?''

She explained it as if she were reading my mind.

``What kind of grades they get, what clubs they do, what kind of friends they have, what they do outside of school---and if you want the finer details, even what kind of drink they'll choose at a cafe. Rational, dependable kids don't have many fluctuations, so they're really easy to collect data on.''

Seriously---what even is this person?

``\dots\dots So you were the one who made the plan during new member recruitment to steer me and Mizasaki into the Biology Club, too?''

``Of course.''

In front of me, the Spring Blend just kept cooling. Senpai drank her cafe latte.

``By the way, where did you catch on, Delchi?''

``It started with a highlighter. The one that was used to mark Euler's identity in Mikage's math magazine was a highlighter neither Mikage nor Mikage-senpai uses. You bought that magazine, marked Euler's identity, and gave it to Mikage. And then you used Mikage-senpai to convince Mikage. Am I wrong?''

``Aya-chii, you already told him that?''

Hongo-senpai shot Mikage a look of exasperation.

``Yes. You didn't tell me not to.''

Mikage replied flatly with something that sounded like a grade-school technicality. She hadn't been moving purely on Hongo-senpai's orders---she seemed to have something of her own in her chest. Hongo-senpai shrugged, like \textit{good grief}.

I pressed on.

``And the poster that was put up in front of the biology room---that was you too.''

``Yup. Because if it wasn't there, people might think you weren't even doing recruitment in the first place. Even if Aya-chii brought you guys there, you'd be in trouble if you didn't have an excuse to go into the biology room, right?''

That biology room had had zero welcoming atmosphere. What got Mikage to drag us in was, undeniably, that poster. She had thought even that far ahead?

``But I didn't think you'd notice that. Why? Did the cover design end up looking kind of similar to that crappy booklet I handed you?''

So she really had deliberately given us a shoddy booklet during recruitment.

But that wasn't the point right now.

``Tokumura-sensei said that poster was made by the current third-years. But Karato-senpai is apparently bad with computers. Only someone used to designing could make something that polished.''

``Eh, maybe Rouchi reused old data and put in an order for it.''

``That poster had a photo worked into the layout---a light-blue budgerigar that came here after last year's Golden Week. It wasn't just swapping out the text. It was designed specifically for this year's recruitment. And it was done by someone who isn't even in the Biology Club. The only people with a reason to be that meddlesome are you guys.''

Hongo-senpai nodded, looking convinced.

``I see. Well, you're right, but I don't like `meddlesome.' For the sake of the Biology Club---another science club---and for my best friend who's completely lost her motivation, it's only natural that I'd do that much.''

If it were just that I made a poster and helped with recruitment for a friend who'd lost her drive, it would sound nice. But the plan this senpai had built was far more petty than that.

She had ordered Mikage to guide Mizasaki and me into solving the equation mystery, and by a far more roundabout---but effective---method than simply recommending the Biology Club, she got us to join it.

And then---

``And you were the one who told Kannabi that we'd joined the Biology Club.''

``Oh, so you already know that much.''

Senpai took another delicious-looking sip of her cafe latte, and urged us to drink our coffee too. I drank to wet my throat, but I could barely taste it.

``Did Nabichi say my name?''

In her tone, I felt a faint chill---something frightening, like she was trying to sniff out a traitor---and I shook my head.

``No. Kannabi just said `the Shiji-yaku.'''

Hongo-senpai suddenly burst out laughing.

``Ahaha---seriously? `Shiji-yaku'! That's the same idea as senpai's.''

``The senpai who called you Indie?''

``Yeah, yeah. Kashiwabara-senpai---the previous Chemistry Club President. Like me, she was also Student Council Vice President, and\dots\ well, she was something else too, but she gave me this slightly stylish nickname. I guess she wanted to say I'm some wicked woman who uses the people around her as pawns.''

So that was it.

Indie---no, indicator.

The reason Hongo-senpai said it was a nickname that only worked within the Chemistry Club was because it was a stupid joke built on a chemistry term. And the meaning of indicator---something that indicates---wasn't a gauge or display here.

It had been a blind spot, but there was a more appropriate, far more convincing equivalent.

In a chemistry context, ``indicator'' means---

An indicator reagent.

In other words, a ``thing that points the way.''

And if you swap the kanji---

Shiji-yaku. A ``ringleader.''

It was a word that had been showing up a lot lately in the context of special fraud schemes and shady job rings: the mastermind who draws up the plan and moves people around. For someone like her, it really did fit.

Fear filled my chest before anger did.

A feeling close to awe---at the intellect and boldness that had actually made all of this happen.

``You egged Mizasaki on so that Iwama and I would get to know each other, ordered Mikage to get Mizasaki and me to join the Biology Club, and used Kannabi to push Iwama forward. Is that what you're saying?''

I felt like I'd been used as a part in a PythagoraSwitch contraption. As one component in a clever device designed to drop a marble into its target, this Shiji-yaku moved other people around.

``Well, if you put it simply, yeah, that's about it.''

She said it lightly.

``Why---why would you do that? Wasn't it enough to just help with recruitment? Why did it have to be us?''

``Because the Biology Club and Rouchi are already in that state, right? If you did it normally, there's no way capable kids would ever choose a place like that. I figured if we didn't get exceptionally capable students to join, the Biology Club's glorious tradition was basically finished.''

Exceptionally capable---being told that here didn't make me happy in the slightest.

``So before you even enrolled, I picked you four---who looked like you could revive the Biology Club---and decided you'd join it. Not just top grades: you also participated in science clubs in middle school, and the four of you were highly likely to choose biology. Honestly, Delchi and Riochi were the kind of talent I'd love to secure for the Chemistry Club too.''

Ridiculous. What did she think we were?

``You can't---We have our own will, too, and you're treating us like it's some kind of draft meeting!''

Hongo-senpai laughed again.

``Ahaha, that's funny. A draft meeting? But in the end, you're the ones who chose the Biology Club, right? Only you had the right to choose. You came together of your own free will.''

I had nothing to say to that. She was right. We were the ones who chose. But---

``\dots\dots Came together?''

Without thinking, I said what was on my mind. The discomfort was that strong.

``Wait. The order's wrong. We were already together in the first place.''

I didn't miss the slight movement from Mikage beside me.

``Out of six classes in our grade, the four of us are in the same class. And on top of that, Kannabi, Iwama, and I have consecutive attendance numbers---so you're telling me that the students who happened to meet the conditions you wanted for new club members just happened to be gathered together like this? And even Mikage ended up in the same class.''

If you tried to find suitable candidates within a single class, would it really work out this neatly? Even if it were just ``science-track,'' that would be one thing, but students who planned to choose biology were a minority to begin with.

And Hongo-senpai had said she picked us before we enrolled. If she really chose us beforehand, then this class assignment would have to be an unbelievably lucky coincidence.

``Ah---so you noticed after all.''

Senpai softly set her cup down.

``Not that Mizacchi did, but once I noticed that both Delchi and Riochi have surnames that start with `I,' I thought, Yeah, this is the only way. So I made it so you two would be in the same class, with seats close to each other.''

\dots\dots Hold on.

``As for picking Nabichi, sure, it's because she's a good kid, but also because her surname was the kind that wouldn't be strange to end up with an attendance number close to you two. It's just a coincidence that Mizacchi and Aya-chii are close. Well, that happened to work out nicely for seating, too.''

Stop saying absurd things.

``Wait---this is about class assignment. How can you, as just a student---''

``I'm not just a student. Student Council Vice President. You heard it from my boyfriend, right? At Tsunanagai High School, outstanding students are given that kind of authority and discretion. Typically, the Student Council President is the one who takes the lead, and the Vice President is the one who runs the operation. I'm basically the brains.''

My thoughts couldn't keep up.

In my daze, I vaguely remembered something. Maybe that was what ``Tsunanagai High School's best couple'' meant. I'd wondered what ``best'' even meant, but---Student Council President and Vice President would make sense. Or maybe it referred to grades. I'd heard Mikage-senpai was second in the year. Maybe Hongo-senpai was first.

A monster. That word floated up in my mind.

A Shiji-yaku who used the authority she'd been given and achieved her goals with an exceptional command ability---

But no matter how you looked at it, that was absurd.

Class assignment. Even if someone was outstanding, it wasn't something you let a student do.

When I fell silent, Hongo-senpai spoke first.

``Even the Vice-principal complained, you know. Putting four people whose surnames start with `I' into the same class was a bit much. But seat positions and group assignments in class are important, so I pushed it through anyway. Now that you know how seriously I was thinking about this, can you understand, Delchi?''

My mind felt like it was turning white. So she had even gone as far as manipulating cause and effect.

So that Iwama would end up in the very back seat, and talk to me.

So that Iwama and Kannabi would end up in the same group in class, and deepen their connection.

Not just our class---was she saying even our attendance numbers had been decided by the will of this one student, Hongo Nagisa?

All for the sake of getting the four of us into the Biology Club. A layout designed to drop the marble where it needed to go.

``Did the teachers\dots\ know about this?''

``Some important people did, of course. In the end, it's the school that makes the final call, not me. But they all agreed. They said it couldn't be helped if it was for the sake of protecting the Biology Club.''

``That's impossible. For the sake of keeping a single club alive.''

``A single club?''

Hongo-senpai's voice dropped---her volume stayed the same, but her presence sharpened.

``Even though it's one corner of the clubs that are permitted to boldly call themselves a `Science Division' in this high school---a school that prides itself on tradition going back to the old First Middle School system and puts real effort into science education? This isn't the same as some casual circle or a little friends' club. A lot of researchers have come out of this Biology Club. Your father is one of them, and even the mayor here---he's not a researcher, but he's a Biology Club alumnus too.''

I hadn't expected my father to come up. She really had looked into things thoroughly.

Senpai's voice gradually took on heat.

``Tradition is a giant. Only because there's this massive accumulation built by the people before us can we stand on their shoulders and look down at the world. A school club might seem trivial, and sure, it's small---but it's still a giant. The school wanted to protect that small giant. And I absolutely couldn't accept my best friend being forced into a situation where she'd be treated like the culprit who killed that giant.''

``Even so\dots\ does that mean it's acceptable to manipulate us by pulling tricks like that?''

``Tricks? That's a bit---an unfortunate way to put it.''

Hongo-senpai seemed to think for a moment, then, with a serious look, said:

``There are no tricks in youth. There's only someone's struggle---and the reasons that made them struggle.''

All of a sudden she dragged in a concept like ``youth,'' and her sheer selfishness started to make me angry, too. Were we nothing more than a stage mechanism moved around to realize the upperclassmen's glorious youth?

Maybe she sensed my indignation, because Hongo-senpai looked at me as if to soothe me.

``Well, that's something I borrowed from Kashiwabara-senpai, though. It's a corny line, right? But in a way it's true. All I did was use everything I had and do everything I could so I wouldn't turn my irreplaceable best friend into a murderer. No matter what you think of that effort, I'm sure Rouchi would call it precious.''

In senpai's case, though, what she ``had'' was far too much. And so was what she ``could do.''

I couldn't say I didn't understand what she was trying to say. But even if she had a reasonable motive, even if it was ``just'' her way of struggling---hadn't she trampled something important?

``I understand your motive. But---''

But this, at least, had to be said.

``What happens to our will? If you hadn't engineered this, we would've chosen different paths. And you, as an upperclassman, twisted that with a scheme---and the school approved it.''

``It's not like we twisted it out of spite. We just put everyone where they fit best, and gently pushed them forward. We simply protected something that might have vanished through disorder or coincidence---by using order and inevitability.''

Order and inevitability---scheme or not, we had ended up in the place we belonged.

Maybe she was right. I did think I was glad I joined the Biology Club.

But if that was true, then why? Why was I this furious?

``Okay, so---an analogy.''

Senpai began to speak.

``Once upon a time, there was a traveler. Walking down a country road, he came to a fork. The left path was muddy, so the traveler chose the right.''

The traveler was me, and the roads were my choices.

``What awaited him was a long flight of stone steps. The traveler steeled himself and climbed in one go. Up ahead was a half-collapsed torii gate---a deserted shrine. When he passed through the torii, a blue snake spoke to him.''

Hongo-senpai briefly stuck out her tongue and wet her lips.

``The snake said, `I made that muddy patch.' `I blocked the road because I wanted you to come here.' Now then---does the traveler, outraged, go back down the steps, or does he pass through the shrine and continue onward?''

I considered it. If it were me---

``If that traveler were me, I'd keep going. I don't have a fixed destination, so I'm not particularly attached---I'd just take the path the snake chose.''

``Right. Good.''

Only then did I realize what my fury truly was.

``But what about Iwama?''

``Riochi? She'd take the snake's path more than anyone.''

``Yes, I think so too. She wouldn't go back down the steps---she's not the kind of person who can.''

``I think so too.''

``But that's exactly why what the snake---what you---did is a desecration of the way Iwama lives.''

Maybe it was a line she hadn't expected, because Hongo-senpai didn't respond.

``Iwama was struggling. Whether she should prioritize the life people around her wanted, or the life she wanted for herself---she agonized over it\dots\ and then she was happy that she could finally make a decision for herself. Maybe her parents and friends wouldn't want it. But she was truly glad she joined the Biology Club.''

``Yeah. I know that.''

``If she learned that even that decision was exactly what you wanted, what do you think Iwama would feel?''

Discovering the Inome, meeting Kannabi---someone she could truly hit it off with---and then meeting Mizasaki and me. If she learned that everything she'd rejoiced over as a miracle was, in fact, the plotting of a snake named Hongo Nagisa---what would Iwama feel?

What would happen to that smile she'd worn so innocently?

Seeing how worked up I was, Hongo-senpai tilted her head slightly.

``What would she feel? Of course she'd be shocked. That's why I called you here today, Delchi. If you reached the truth together with Riochi, I thought everything might end up ruined.''

``That's\dots\ what do you mean?''

``The reason I got ahead of it and told you everything today is---of course---so you'll keep quiet.''

I had no words.

``Well, as for this whole thing---Riochi still doesn't know. There's no way she would. She hasn't been told the fact that Mizacchi heard about the collapsed cherry-heart incident from me, she hasn't seen the fluorescent-pen frame around Euler's identity, and the poster in front of the biology room has already been taken down ages ago. If nobody says anything, she won't know.''

``\dots\dots So you're telling me not to tell her.''

``Yup. If you and Nabichi cooperate, we should be able to keep it hidden. It's not hard. You notice the little details, Delchi, and Nabichi's good at lying. Could you do that for me?''

I thought about it. If we kept Hongo-senpai's plan secret, would Iwama be able to stay happy?

Seeing me hesitate, Hongo-senpai wore a faint smile. She was probably expecting that after some wavering, I'd make a bitter face and say, ``Understood.''

And maybe that was the right path.

Iwama was satisfied with how things were now. She'd been happy that she could make a decision for herself. So for me to come along and expose it with, ``Actually, there was something going on behind the scenes,'' would be completely unnecessary.

I knew that well myself. I didn't live in a way where I involved myself in other people's lives enough to choose an action that could saddle me with responsibility---responsibility serious enough to ruin Iwama's happiness if I handled it wrong.

But---

Living happily on top of soil with a secret buried underneath wasn't a scientific attitude at all.

``I'm going to tell her.''

``Huh?''

At my answer---one she surely hadn't expected---Hongo-senpai's eyebrows twitched just slightly.

``I'm going to tell Iwama everything.''

``Why?''

``Because she isn't someone who can be happy with lies and secrets.''

The private room fell into silence for a while. Senpai's expression hardened, and the carefree gyaru vibe vanished.

``\dots\dots You're going to expose the truth, and then you can take responsibility for it? You're fine with Riochi living her whole life with that bitterness lodged in her chest after she learns the truth?''

``Yes. I'll take on that `responsibility.' After telling her everything, if Iwama still chooses to join the Biology Club---''

Softly,

``I'll make Iwama happy.''

The words slipped out of my mouth with shocking ease.

Only after saying them did I realize what I'd just blurted out.

After that, I couldn't say anything, and Hongo-senpai looked at me with a faint crease between her brows.

``Then,''

The one who broke the silence was Mikage.

``I will tell Iwama-san the truth\dots\dots I believe that is the very least sincerity we can show her, after using her for our own convenience.''

I looked at Mikage.

Still expressionless as always, Mikage nodded at me.

The next day at lunch, Mikage spoke to Iwama. She said something like asking if she wanted to eat lunch together, and the two of them left the classroom. All I could do was watch their backs.

When Iwama returned to the classroom around the end of lunch, she didn't look particularly shocked.

But after school---

``Hey, Del-chan, wanna walk home together again today?''

She invited me. This wasn't the time to worry about what Mizasaki or Kannabi might think. I nodded, and the two of us hurried out of school.

It wasn't like we were doing anything wrong, but we veered off the usual route to school and, on a whim, hopped on a bus heading toward the station. We sat in the very back. With no plan at all, I didn't even really know what I wanted to do. Since it wasn't a commuter route, no other Tsunanagai High School students got on.

This bus line didn't go through the station-front shopping street---it kept going to the next station instead. I considered getting off at the station-front shopping street entrance, but then we'd just have taken a detour by bus for a route we could have walked anyway. Iwama didn't stand up, so I stayed where I was too, sitting beside her with about half a person's worth of space between us.

``So, what do we do?''

As I said it while looking at Tsunanagai Station growing farther away---

``Until the last stop.''

Iwama smiled faintly.

Inside the bus, a few elderly passengers sat quietly here and there. Somehow we kept our voices down, and we got off at the last stop, Koshizaki Station. The moment we stepped off the bus, bright sunlight poured straight down from a deep blue sky.

Koshizaki was a small station downhill---opposite the direction of the Ebikawa that Iwama used and the Sunamizu that Kannabi used. It wasn't really a place you'd go out of your way to stop by, so it was my first time there too. There were barely any people around.

Iwama looked around with clear enjoyment, then started walking. I followed along at an easy pace. We crossed a railroad crossing and entered a huge park built within a seaside pine grove.

``Have you been here before?''

``Nope, not at all.''

``Then did someone recommend it?''

``No. This is a decision that's just ours.''

That was good.

The wind was a little strong, but the ocean view was great. Beneath a sky of solid blue, the Pacific spread out in a darker blue. Here and there, a few white yachts floated.

We'd left right after school, so the sun was still high. The clear blue sky felt strangely comforting.

``This feels so good.''

Iwama spread her arms wide to the sea breeze. Behind her, I mimicked her a little. The cool wind fluttered our uniforms. When I took a deep breath, there was a faint scent of salt.

We bought carbonated drinks from a vending machine and, little by little, drank while looking at the ocean on a bench where Japanese red pines blocked the wind and sunlight.

Bit by bit, we started the conversation we needed to have.

Iwama said she'd been told the truth by Mikage. If I asked how much, it would just be stirring up trouble, so I didn't say much from my side.

``So basically, they wanted me to join the Biology Club, and the senpai came up with all kinds of plans for me, right?''

`Came up with for you'\dots\ or more like, `came up with,' or\dots''

Iwama nodded and turned toward me.

``Mikage-san said she decided to join the Chemistry Club instead of the Physics Club.''

That was news to me.

``Seriously? I assumed she'd join the Physics Club\dots\ Her older brother's there, and she said she liked math.''

``So what? She said she chose Chemistry because she wanted to overturn what the senpai expected. And when she said that, her older brother apparently cried.''

So he cries, huh---that guy.

``I see. Overturn what they expected\dots''

I understood the feeling. She probably wanted to put at least a small scratch on the outcome of ``everything went exactly the way the upperclassmen wanted.'' Even while being used, Mikage had made a small act of rebellion.

Iwama spoke carefully.

``Mikage-san told me. She said you got angry for my sake, Del-chan.''

So she told her that much.

For a moment, I thought: \textit{Please tell me she didn't also repeat that arrogant line about me making Iwama happy.}

Not knowing what to say, I took a sip of cola. The clean sweetness that didn't linger slid over my tongue. The fizz dissolved a little of my embarrassment.

``\dots\dots Thank you. When I heard that, I was really happy.''

``It's not like\dots\ I got angry for your sake. I just thought she was doing something awful, so I said she'd done something awful---that's all.''

Iwama laughed a little.

``There aren't many people who get genuinely angry for me. Most people are like, you're on the right path, so you should hold your head high\dots\ I'm grateful, but it's always stuff like that.''

From that alone, I could almost see Iwama's pain.

It was a world I couldn't even imagine, but I tried to think it through.

For someone you see as an idol or a hero---someone who walks proudly in the sun, an overwhelmingly strong person---who would get angry for them?

I'd known Iwama was struggling. I'd seen the small weakness she showed. Wasn't that why I'd gotten angry?

If it were for cherry blossoms blooming proudly in the sun, with complete confidence\dots\ would it have been the same?

``Having to keep your head up all the time\dots\ that sounds exhausting.''

``Maybe.''

Iwama was drinking C.C. Lemon. When she twisted off the cap, it made a small \textit{pssh}.

``You still haven't turned in your membership form, right?''

``Yeah.''

``So\dots\ you can still go back, if you want.''

I tilted my head a little and looked at Iwama beside me.

``Even if you don't join the Biology Club, I'm not going to be upset. Mizasaki won't either. Kannabi would understand. I think it wouldn't be bad to rethink everything from scratch.''

Iwama looked at me with a slightly sad expression.

``So if I don't join, you won't be lonely, Del-chan?''

Her words caught me off guard, and I could tell I was flustered.

``Ah---no, that's\dots\ I mean, maybe a little\dots''

``Sorry. Just kidding.''

What a nasty joke. I was talking seriously.

``I'm happy you said it's okay to rethink it, but\dots\ I'm still going to join the Biology Club.''

``\dots\dots Even after you learned the truth?''

``Yeah. I mean, stuff like that happens in life all the time, doesn't it? No matter what you choose, there'll always be at least a little blemish on it.''

``I see.''

That was an awfully clear-cut way of thinking. She was probably a lot more mature than I was.

With the sea breeze tossing her bangs, Iwama drank her C.C. Lemon like it was delicious.

``I'm sure the senpai were right---I think the Biology Club suits me. And besides, right now I really, really feel like I want to do investigations and research together with everyone.''

``\dots\dots Then I'm glad.''

I didn't say it out loud, but I felt the same way.

If I could do research together with Iwama---someone who knew a world I didn't---there was no doubt it would be fun.

After taking in more than enough sea breeze, we headed to Koshizaki Station. Since Iwama could get home just by riding from there, we decided to take the train back on the return trip.

The station building was unmanned. It was so run-down you'd never guess it was right next to Tsunanagai Station. Still, from the plastic benches set up on the platform, you could see the ocean beyond the tracks. We still had time until the next train, so we sat there and sipped the rest of our carbonated drinks little by little.

``By the way\dots\ I tried making a pressed-leaf specimen.''

Iwama brought it up suddenly.

``Of the katakuri?''

``Yeah.''

I remembered giving her the katakuri we'd dug up that day we went to see the cherry blossoms. Not even in a bouquet---soil still on the bulb, shoved into a used convenience-store plastic bag and handed over. Even now, I sometimes regretted what a stupid thing that was to do.

``\dots\dots So you didn't throw it away.''

``Huh? Of course I didn't! If anything, I'd eat it before I threw it away.''

That wasn't what I'd meant. When I laughed without thinking, Iwama looked at me as if I were strange.

``Sorry. I just\dots\ wondered if it was a hassle, getting handed something like that by someone you'd barely even met.''

``It wasn't a hassle at all. I tried it myself afterward, but digging up katakuri roots is really hard\dots\ I ended up respecting you, Del-chan, for digging it up like it was nothing.''

There was a trick to it, but explaining it here would probably just be unnecessary.

``If it helped at all, I'm honored.''

``Yeah. Thanks.''

Iwama stared at the ocean for a while, then turned her face slightly toward me.

``Del-chan, do you know the katakuri's flower language?''

``\dots\dots No, I don't.''

And only after saying it did I realize: with that idiotic act, hadn't I technically ``given'' Iwama a flower? Even if it wasn't ``suffering for generations,'' the thought of there being some weird flower meaning made my blood run cold.

``Um\dots\ sorry. I really wasn't thinking about flower meanings or anything.''

``I know. I figured you weren't.''

Iwama giggled, and then---

``Enduring loneliness.''

She said it slowly, like she was savoring the words.

``That's the katakuri's flower language?''

``Yeah. For eight whole years after it sprouts, katakuri only spreads its leaves in spring and spends the rest of the time storing nutrients underground. From summer through winter, it's in the soil. If it doesn't bloom, insects won't come, and nobody even notices it. Supposedly, the way katakuri still endures all that and blooms anyway is where the flower language comes from.''

``I see. So that's---''

``Scientific!''

I hadn't been trying to set her up, but somehow it came out like I had.

``That's why I was happy, too. In that sense.''

``\dots\dots In what sense?''

Iwama hesitated a little, then opened her mouth with a shy sort of smile.

``Like\dots\ maybe now I can finally bloom too.''

Just then, the station announcement began---\textit{Now arriving\dots}---and I lost the words to respond. But maybe that was for the best.

I remembered the words I'd seen written on an ema before I ever met Iwama.

---In high school, please let me do things well.

If she'd written ``in high school,'' then there must have been something she hadn't been able to do well before. In middle school, Iwama had probably gone through a bitter experience. Something in her past that corresponded to the eight years katakuri spent underground.

But I still didn't have the courage to dig that up yet.

\fullpageimage{8.jpg}


\thispagestyle{plain}

\vspace{1cm}

``Let's do our best.''

``Yeah!''

That was about all I could say to her.

Then we heard the clatter of wheels. At last, the train came in along the seaside tracks.

The deep Turnbull's blue of the ocean surface sparkled cheerfully beneath the blue sky.

Looks like today, we'll be able to make it home while it's still light.

% ==============================
%        Epilogue
% ==============================
\clearpage
\thispagestyle{plain}
\phantomsection
\begin{center}
    \large\bfseries
    Epilogue\\
    The Winter of College Entrance Exams Is Short
\end{center}
\label{sec:epilogue}
\addcontentsline{toc}{chapter}{Epilogue}
\vspace{1cm}

Of the three years of high school, I thought the winter of university entrance exams felt especially short. It was already March.

There were probably things I should be doing, but until the results were posted, I just couldn't bring myself to focus. In the early afternoon, I went to Iwama's house as invited. When I pressed the doorbell, the front door opened almost immediately.

``Good work! Come in!''

It was a neat detached house. I'd been there a few times, but the number of shoes lined up at the entryway was the smallest I'd ever seen. Or rather, there were only the shoes Iwama had slipped on to open the door, and my own.

As if she'd guessed what I was thinking from where my eyes went, Iwama scratched her head.

``Today, I only invited you, Del-chan\dots\ The other two are still studying, I think.''

So it was just the two of us. I couldn't even begin to count how many times I'd been caught in this pattern over the last three years. It was probably my own fault for going out so readily without checking who else would be there, but still.

``Where are your parents?''

``At work. My mom went out for a meeting too.''

``Huh\dots''

Even as I wondered why she'd let me in under those circumstances, I followed her up to her room on the second floor.

Iwama's room didn't feel very lived-in. It was practically like a model room. Aside from the terrifying number of books and reference materials crammed into her desk and bookshelf, there was nothing beyond the bare minimum.

We chatted for a while as I drank the Earl Grey she made for me.

``Today, there's something I want to show you.''

With that, we left her room together. Iwama stopped in front of a door across the hall.

``A storage room?''

``Nope. A secret room.''
